---

# **COMMUTED HIRES THEIR ARCHIVIST**

---

## **INT.  KENDALL’S APARTMENT – WASHINGTON, D.C. – NIGHT – MARCH 1998**

Tiny place.  One-bedroom rental in Dupont that smells like boxed wine and regret.  Kendall sits on the floor, cordless phone in hand, laptop open to an empty email inbox.  She’s barefoot.  Sweatpants.  UT hoodie.  Hair in a bun that’s lost all structural integrity.  She stares at the number she still had scribbled in an old Rolodex.  *Jim Brown (DRUMS – chaos man)*

She dials.

**RING.**

**RING.**

**[[4.4 JIM BROWN character bible|JIM]]** (V.O.)
“Yeah?”

His voice is rough.  Loud.  Somewhere between backstage and drunk.  Someone yells *“Jesus, turn that down!”* in the background.

**[[5.5 Kendall Weatherby|KENDALL]]**
“Hey.  It’s Kendall Weatherby.”

Silence.  Like the world actually stopped breathing.

Then:

**JIM**
“…From the bar in D.C.  with the mirror?”

**KENDALL** (laughs once, short)
“That’s the one.  I—uh.  I hope this isn’t a weird time.”

**JIM**
“You kidding?  You could’ve called during a volcano.  What’s up?”

She shifts.  Doesn’t want to sound fragile.  Or desperate.  Or turned on.

**KENDALL**
“So.  I made a… professional change recently.  I’m out of government.”

**JIM** (beat)
“No shit.”

**KENDALL**
“No shit.”

Another pause.

**JIM**
“Sorry—are congratulations in order?  Or condolences?”

**KENDALL** (sips bourbon, dry)
“We’re still in the autopsy phase.”

Beat.

**KENDALL** (cont’d)
“Anyway, I’m looking at options.  And I remembered you saying… if I ever needed anything…”

**JIM** (quiet now)
“I meant it.”

She swallows.

**KENDALL**
“Right.  Well.  If your band is still a band, and you’re in need of a literate, type-A media wrangler with a master's degree and a mild disregard for reality…”

Beat.

**KENDALL** (cont’d)
“I’m available.”

Silence.

Then laughter.  Not mocking—*relieved.*

**JIM**
“Jesus.  I’ve been waiting two years to hear you ask for anything.  I was starting to think I dreamed you.”

**KENDALL**
“Don’t make it weird.”

**JIM**
“Never.”

Beat.

**JIM**
“You free Friday?”

**KENDALL**
“I can be.”

**JIM**
“Good.  We’re in Chicago.  I’ll get you a flight.  You’ll hate the hotel.  Bring red nail polish.”

**KENDALL**
“Strictly professional, Jim.”

**JIM**
“I know.  I’m just nostalgic.”

She smiles.  Just a little.  Nobody sees it.

**KENDALL**
“See you Friday.”

She hangs up.  Then mutters to herself, into the empty apartment: “Still got it.”

---

**EXCERPT – KENDALL WEATHERBY’S DIARY – MARCH 17, 1998**

**LOCATION**: Dupont Circle apartment
**WEATHER**: Cold snap.  Gray.  Uninspiring.
**MOOD**: Tired.  Determined.  Pissed off at my own optimism.

**NOTABLE ACTION**: Called Jim Brown today.

First voice I’ve heard in weeks that didn’t sound like it wanted to spin me or seduce me.  I didn’t flirt.  He didn’t beg.  It was cleaner than I expected.

I told him I needed work.  That’s a sentence I never thought I’d write down.  But it’s true.  No salary.  No fallback.  I nuked my own political trajectory and all I have to show for it is bourbon breath and five freelance offers from think tanks that treat genocide like a branding opportunity.

Jim said yes.  No hesitation.  Booked the flight while I was still talking.  Either he’s desperate or he remembers me better than I thought.

I said it was professional.  He didn’t argue.  I didn’t mean it.

(Edit this entry before anyone reads it.  Or don’t.  Let the biographers deal with it.)

---

## **INT.  UNITED CENTER – BACKSTAGE SERVICE CORRIDOR – CHICAGO – MARCH 1998 – NIGHT**

The fluorescent lights buzz like they've been screaming for years.  Cables snake across the floor.  A forklift groans somewhere down the hall.  The air smells like dried beer, concrete, and the burnt ozone of too many amps.

**Kendall**, trench coat on, red nails sharp as ever, stands with a battered leather satchel over her shoulder.  She looks like she’s ready to fire someone.  Or run for Senate.  Or both.  **Jim Brown** approaches from the other end.  Hoodie, jeans, boots scuffed from load-in.  He slows when he sees her.

**JIM** (low, almost too casual)
Hey.

**KENDALL**
Evening.

They’re three feet apart.  He gestures to a side alcove with less foot traffic—two folding chairs and a utility sink.  The glamour of rock and roll.  They move into the space.  He sits.  She stands.

**JIM** (sincere)
Thanks for coming.

**KENDALL**
I figured it beat starvation.

He chuckles, but it doesn’t stick.

**JIM**
Look.  Before we do anything official—I just want to ask.  *What do you want out of this?*

**KENDALL**
A paycheck.

**JIM**
That can’t be all.

**KENDALL** (matter-of-fact)
Something real wouldn’t hurt.  I spent four years writing lies for men in better suits than sense.  If I’m going to organize chaos, I’d rather do it for people who admit they’re animals.

**JIM** (nods)
That we are.

She finally sits.  Legs crossed.  Calm.

**JIM**
And you know this can’t get…  complicated.

**KENDALL**
Oh, I assumed you were still paranoid about falling in love with me.

**JIM** (flat)
No.  I’m paranoid about *hurting the only woman I’ve met who made me want to be decent.*

That silences her.  Just for a beat.

**JIM**
You burned into me.  And then you left.  So now you’re back.  I need to know if this is a job—or a door.

**KENDALL** (firm)
This is a job.

**JIM**
Even if it becomes something else?

She looks him dead in the eye.

**KENDALL**
Then we both act like grown-ups.  I’m here to work, not relive a fever dream.  That part?  It was great.  I won’t pretend otherwise.  But I need this to be clean.

**JIM** (quiet)
Yeah.  Me too.

Silence.  Then:

**KENDALL**
Though for the record…I never left you.  I left D.C.  You just got caught in the blast radius.

She stands.

**KENDALL**
Now show me where the bodies are buried.  If I’m going to help this band survive, I need every dirty secret on file by Thursday.

He smiles—grateful, cautious, maybe a little doomed.

**JIM**
Welcome to the circus.

---

## **INT.  UNITED CENTER – BACKSTAGE – MOMENTS LATER**

**Kendall** follows Jim through a metal double door and into the **production corridor** behind the main stage.  The hum of tension is thick.

Then—shouting.

**PYRO MIKE** (not subtle)
I’M TELLING YOU, IF WE DON’T TRIPLE THE CHARGES ON “SPEEDING,” NO ONE’S GONNA FEEL THE DROP!

**LASER TECH** (screaming back)
IF YOU TRIPLE THE PYRO, IT’LL LOOK LIKE A TRASH FIRE IN A FOG MACHINE!  WE’LL LOSE THE ENTIRE LIGHT SEQUENCE!

**PYRO MIKE**
I GOT SIXTEEN CAKES READY TO GO!

**LASER TECH**
YOU’LL BURN OUT THE GREEN DIODES, YOU LUNATIC!

**Kendall** stops, looks at Jim.  Blinking.  Calm.  Then **Bill**—shirt half-buttoned, still chewing a piece of gum the color of roadkill—barges in from the opposite side of the corridor.

**[[4.1 BILL DAVENPORT character bible|BILL]]** (amped)
Okay, I’ve decided we open with **“Sirius.”**  Because, I mean, c’mon—it’s the United Center.  *It’s Jordan season, baby!*

The laser tech *actually groans.* The pyro guy does a fist pump like he just won a custody battle.

**KENDALL** (sotto, to Jim)
Is this another day at the office?

**JIM** (grinning, resigned)
Yup.

A rigging cable drops with a loud *CLANK* behind them.  Neither one flinches.

**KENDALL**
Okay.  I need a list of songs that cause spontaneous combustion and a seating chart for all emotionally unstable staff.  Also, do we have a safe word?

**JIM**
Just scream “Cremeans.” That usually resets everyone.

**KENDALL**
Noted.

She straightens her coat.  Then steps forward.

**KENDALL** (excited, to no one in particular)
Alright, gentlemen—let’s burn this building down *professionally.*

---

## **INT.  UNITED CENTER – BACKSTAGE CHAOS – SAME MOMENT**

Kendall watches two techs nearly come to blows over dry ice limits.  Someone yells something about *“scorch radius compliance.”* A runner sprints by with a crate of Diet Coke and one singular tambourine.

**KENDALL** (flat)
So.  I work here now?

**JIM** (throwing his arms up)
Do you think I have *hiring authority*?  I’m just the **drummer!**

A pyro charge goes off in the rafters—just a test—and the boom echoes like a small war.

**KENDALL** (surveys the carnage)
Well, lucky for you… I’m amazingly comfortable assuming power I wasn’t officially given.

**JIM** (grinning)
That’s why I called you.

She pats his shoulder and walks off like she owns the damn tour.

**JIM** (to himself, shaking his head)
God help us all.

---

## **INT.  UNITED CENTER – DRESSING ROOM ANNEX – NIGHT**

They’ve moved into a quieter space.  Slightly quieter.  A cracked mirror.  A couch that might’ve been white in 1987.  A strong smell of menthol and someone’s anxiety sweat.  **Jim** leans against the wall, arms folded. **Kendall** has her notebook out but doesn’t bother writing yet.  She’s absorbing.

**JIM**
Alright.  Here’s how this goes.

**KENDALL**
Is there a contract?

**JIM**
Eventually.  Maybe.  But first—we do the trial by fire.

**KENDALL**
Of course we do.

**JIM**
You’ve got four interviews.  One’s formal.  The other three are emotional hostage negotiations.

**KENDALL**
Naturally.

**JIM**
First, you talk to **Jeff Cremeans**.  He’s the manager.  You’ll technically report to him.  He’ll pretend he doesn’t remember your name.  He’ll be assessing you.

**KENDALL**
Got it.  Play polite.  Don’t blink.

**JIM**
Then you get **Kathy.** She’s the lead singer.  You’ll like her.  A lot.  She won’t like you.  Much.

**KENDALL**
Great.

**JIM**
She’s brilliant.  Impossible.  She’s also a little territorial.  If she senses you’re trying to control the band’s voice, you’re dead.

**KENDALL**
I control narratives, not people.

**JIM**
Yeah, don’t say that to her.

**KENDALL**
Noted.

**JIM**
Then there’s **Jeff Evans.** Bass.  Human raincloud.  He won’t like you.  You won’t like him.  He’s emotionally post-verbal.  But he’s smart.  Smarter than he looks.  If he says “I guess she’s fine,” that’s a glowing endorsement.

**KENDALL**
And if he doesn’t say anything?

**JIM**
Then he’s plotting your exit.  Fast.

**KENDALL**
Perfect.  And the last step?

**JIM**
Band vote.  Six total.  You need four.

**KENDALL**
And if it’s three-three?

**JIM**
You don’t get hired.  And if you *do* get hired without Kathy or Evans?  They will just make your life so miserable you’ll want to quit.

**KENDALL**
So this is less an interview and more of a diplomatic summit with nuclear options.

**JIM**
Exactly.

She closes her notebook.

**KENDALL**
I’ve handled genocidal defense contractors.  I can manage a lead singer with trust issues.

**JIM**
God, I missed you.

---

## **INT.  UNITED CENTER – DRESSING ROOM ANNEX – NIGHT (CONTINUED)**

Kendall is jotting in her notebook, building her own psychological battlefield guide to Commuted.  Jim leans in, serious now.

**JIM**
One more thing.

**KENDALL**
Let me guess.  There’s a guy named Gilley and he’s the band’s emotional support Tasmanian devil?

**JIM**
Gilley.  Yes.  Guitarist.  Founding member.  Also the reason three publicists have had nervous breakdowns, and one ex-wife had to leave the continent.

**KENDALL**
I’ve read the articles.

**JIM**
The articles are the G-rated version.  Listen—this part’s important.

He shifts.  Voice low.  Not protective, just brutally honest.

**JIM**
If you’re friendly?  Fine.  He’ll flirt.  He flirts with everybody.  But if you show *any* sexual interest, even accidentally—a tilt of the head, a certain kind of laugh, a second-long too-warm eye contact—he will take that as **invitation, challenge, and inevitability.**

**KENDALL**
And what happens then?

**JIM**
He will have you on your back inside of two hours.  And you will not be able to help yourself.  Because Gilley is like Bill Clinton with a Stratocaster and fewer ethics.

**KENDALL** (smiling)
So I should slam the door.

**JIM**
Hard.  Fast.  Immediately.  The first time he crosses the line—shut it down.  He won’t punish you.  He respects clear boundaries.  But if you *ever* leave the door open again, even a crack?

**KENDALL**
He’ll kick it in.

**JIM**
With rhythm.

She nods slowly.

**KENDALL**
Good to know.  I’ll handle it.

**JIM**
Yeah.  You will.

Beat.

**JIM**
He’ll like you, by the way.  Maybe too much.  Just don’t give him poetry.

**KENDALL**
What happens then?

**JIM**
Then he thinks he’s in love.  And that’s a whole other war.

---

## **INT.  UNITED CENTER – BACKSTAGE HALLWAY – MINUTES LATER**

**Kendall** exits the dressing room annex, her notebook tucked under one arm, walking with the confidence of someone who’s already survived the State Department *and* a malfunctioning pyro rehearsal.  From the corner, **Gilley** appears like he was *summoned*.  He struts.  **Wife beater tight.  Pink linen jacket.  Sleeves rolled to the elbow.**  He looks like Don Johnson by way of Memphis.  Aviators perched on his head.  Hair too good to be accidental.  He takes one long look as he walks by.

Eyes move—**up, down, slower than polite.**  Not leering.  Just *assessing.*  Notes her posture, her hair, the sharpness of her shoes.  Also notes: **no ass.  Doesn’t care.** She's got something else—something alive behind the eyes.  He slows.  Smiles.  That **slow, lazy, I-just-woke-up-on-a-yacht** smile.

**[[4.2 JEREMY GILLEY character bible|GILLEY]]** (silken drawl)
Well now.  Who are *you*?

**KENDALL** (pauses, meets his gaze)
Your new HR compliance nightmare.

**GILLEY** (laughs, delighted)
Oh hell.  You *must* be Weatherby.

He takes off the shades, finally—just enough eye contact to suggest he *could* be serious.

**GILLEY**
Jim said you had fire.  He undersold it.

He steps a little closer.  Not predatory.  Just… *aware.*

**GILLEY**
So what’s your role, sugar?  You here to fix us?  Save us?  Ruin us?

**KENDALL** (flashes a razor smile)
None of the above.  I’m just here to write down the damage.

He likes that.  Too much.  Runs a hand through his hair like it's instinct.

**GILLEY**
I’m Gilley.  Guitar.  Mayhem.  Welcome to the band—or the asylum.  Depending on how you take your trauma.

**KENDALL**
Noted.  And just so we’re clear—

She takes one step closer.  Eye to eye now.  Not afraid.  Not amused.  Just *clean, sharp warning.*

**KENDALL**
Flirting’s fine.  Games are fun.  But you make one move beyond this hallway, I will *end your storyline* so fast it’ll make your groupies blink.

Beat.  Gilley grins wider.

**GILLEY**
Goddamn.  I hope you stay.

He walks away.  No retort.  No challenge.  Just that *saunter* like he owns the moonlight.

**KENDALL** (to herself)
Jesus.  He *is* Clinton with guitar strings.

---

## **INT.  BACKSTAGE – SMALL STAGE-LEFT STORAGE ALCOVE – MOMENTS LATER**

Kendall slips out of the hallway after Gilley vanishes into the chaos.  Jim’s already waiting.  Leaning against a stack of black road cases, arms folded, watching her like a dad who just saw the toddler touch the hot stove.

**JIM** (straight-faced)
You realize you said something you shouldn’t have.

**KENDALL** (blinking)
Which part?

**JIM**
You told him flirting’s okay.

**KENDALL**
So?

**JIM** (flatter now)
That means he’s going to make another run at your pussy.

She stares at him.

**KENDALL**
Is he really that precise?

**JIM**
Worse.  He’s *obsessive.*  He logs the moment.  The tone.  The body language.  If you said “flirting’s okay,” he just filed that under “eventual success—proceed with charm escalation.”

**KENDALL**
So he’s a charismatic sociopath?

**JIM**
No.  He’s OCD with a smile and a guitar.  He’s not being creepy.  He’s just wired to complete the mission *you accidentally authorized.*

**KENDALL**
Jesus.

**JIM**
You’ve got one more shot.  Next time he pokes at it—slam the door.  Lock it.  Nail it shut.  If you do, he’ll back off.  He’s weirdly respectful *once you mark the territory.*

**KENDALL**
And if I flirt back again?

**JIM**
Then clear your schedule.  You’ll be naked by soundcheck.

She sighs.

**KENDALL**
Jesus Christ.

**JIM**
Welcome to Commuted.

---

## **INT.  UNITED CENTER – BACKSTAGE GREENROOM – LATER THAT NIGHT**

Jim and Kendall are parked on a battered couch.  The air smells like coffee, weed, and the rubber scent of gear cases.  Kendall’s unspooling her hair from a clip.  Jim sips something from a dented thermos that smells like whiskey and regret.

**JIM**
You read Kathy’s *Playboy* interview?  From about a year and a half ago?

**KENDALL** (squints)
Do I look like someone with time to read *Playboy*?

**JIM**
Fair.  But it wasn’t just the article.  Pictorial too.  Front to back, no apologies.

**KENDALL**
Can’t say I’ve seen it.

**JIM**
It sums her up.  Smart, defiant, bare as hell—literally.  Said more in three photos than most politicians manage in a whole career.  Made the right people nervous.

**KENDALL**
You forget—until a month ago I was working eighty-hour weeks since the ’92 election.  Haven’t read anything that wasn’t a briefing binder or a subcommittee report since the campaign trail.
It’s been policy, policy, policy, and then hearings stacked on hearings until I forgot what sleep felt like.

She leans back, eyes the ceiling.

**KENDALL**
All I knew about Commuted came secondhand.  My ex-boss’s wife said y’all were a bunch of assholes.

**JIM** (grinning)
Tipper?

**KENDALL**
Tipper.

**JIM** (long sip, then deadpan)
The best thing that could happen to Tipper is get hit by lightning.

**KENDALL** (raising an eyebrow)
I’m gonna need context.

**JIM**
She tried to censor the planet one band at a time.  Thought music was a threat to the republic.  Kathy made her sweat.  So did the *Playboy* spread.  She wanted clean.  We gave her sacred filth.

**KENDALL**
And what was the strategy behind that?

**JIM**
No strategy.  Just honesty.  We weren’t built to be safe.  And Kathy?  She didn’t flash skin to titillate.  She did it because she got tired of men like Al writing her body out of the narrative.

**KENDALL** (pauses)
Jesus Christ.  I might actually like her.

**JIM**
You will.  Eventually.  She’ll make you earn it, though.

---

## **INT. KENDALL’S HOTEL ROOM – LATE NIGHT – MARCH 1998**

She’s alone.  Still dressed from the show.  Kicked off one shoe, the other still on.  Legs tucked under her on the scratchy hotel chair.  Laptop open.  Room dim except for the blue-white glow of the screen.  She’s reading.  **Kathy’s Playboy essay.**  Sixteen pictures.  Frontal nudity.  Shaved twat.  One angle’s so sharp it reveals **a hint—*just a goddamn hint***—of clitoris.  Not pornographic.  Not coy.  Just… *there.*  And then the essay: **"Release Me."**

By the time she hits Section VII—**“On Being Hairless in 1995”**—Kendall is frozen.  Not from judgment.  From *awe.*  And maybe, *quiet horror.*  Because this woman—this force of rage, intelligence, sex, trauma, and truth—*is in the band.*  And Kendall’s supposed to collaborate with her.  Archive her.  Translate her to the public.  She leans back, exhales slow.

**KENDALL** (softly, to herself)
What the fuck am I getting into?

Then, after a beat:

**KENDALL**
*What the fuck am I getting into?-

But her mouth is *smiling.*  The kind of smile that knows it’s about to either **burn or bloom**.  Maybe both.  She closes the laptop.  Doesn’t even flinch.

**KENDALL**
Alright, Espich.  Let’s see if you’re as terrifying in person.

---

## **INT.  GUND ARENA – BACKSTAGE SERVICE CORRIDOR – CLEVELAND – MARCH 1998 – AFTERNOON**

**Kendall** stands just off the loading ramp, squinting at a hand-drawn “Band Zone” map taped to a pillar.  Her legal pad is covered in scribbles—tech contacts, crew names, something about power converters—and three boxes she’s labeled “UNCLEAR AUTHORITY.”  She’s muttering to herself.

**KENDALL**
Okay, so Jim reports to Jeff, but Gilley ignores Jeff, and Kathy *technically* doesn’t answer to anyone but also makes all the decisions…

**Then—**

**BOOM.**

A door slams open somewhere behind her.  The sound of *combat boots on concrete* and the unmistakable **voice of revolution wrapped in gasoline.**

**[[4.5 KATHY ESPICH character bible|KATHY]] (O.S.)**
I WANT MY FUCKING MONEY BACK FROM THE DNC!

Kendall turns.  And there she is.

**Kathy Espich.** Five-foot-whatever.  Aviators in her hair.  Sleeveless CBGB tank.  **Eyes like an indictment.** Lipstick already battle-tested.  Fire trailing in her wake.

**KATHY**
I don’t care *how* they send it.  Check, money order, a goddamn bag of singles thrown at my feet—but they will NOT get another *goddamn dime* out of me until they take out the TRASH.

She turns a corner—**bam!** Face-to-face with **Kendall.**

**KATHY** (doesn’t miss a beat)
Who the fuck are you?

**KENDALL** (tight smile)
Internal comms.  Documentation.  PR filter.  Kendall Weatherby.

**KATHY** (eyes her up and down)
You the one Jim dragged in from D.C.?

**KENDALL**
Guilty.

**KATHY**
You a Democrat?

**KENDALL**
Recovering.

**KATHY**
Good.  Then maybe you’ll understand that the entire party’s a fire hazard made of broken promises and industrial-grade bullshit.  Tell ‘em I want my *fucking* money back.  Every last dime I gave for “I feel your pain” and “Man from Hope” and “Kenneth Starr.”  They’ve been listening for six years and all I hear is the sound of women getting steamrolled under polling data.

**KENDALL** (quietly)
Yeah.  I noticed.

Pause.

Kathy sniffs once.  Nods.

**KATHY**
Alright.  You’re not a plant.

(beat)

Now where the fuck is coffee service?  And who do I talk to about getting *fruit that doesn’t look like it lost a custody battle*?

**KENDALL** (pointing)
Stage left hallway.  Take a right at wardrobe.  If the bananas are brown, threaten legal action.

**KATHY** (smiling)
You might actually survive.

She storms off.  Kendall stands there, slightly windblown.

**KENDALL** (to herself)
So that’s the frontwoman.

She jots in her pad: *Espich: Weaponized ideology.  Direct line to rage.  Navigates like a tank in a dress.  Make sure she’s caffeinated before asking for anything.*

---

## **INT.  GUND ARENA – UTILITY STAIRWELL – MOMENTS AFTER THE KATHY ENCOUNTER**

Kendall leans on a stairwell railing, flipping her notepad closed like she’s bracing for turbulence. **Jim** steps in behind her, nursing a coffee that probably has bourbon in it.

**JIM**
So.  You met Kathy.

**KENDALL**
Yup.

**JIM**
And you’re still standing.  That’s good.

**KENDALL**
Barely.

**JIM** (sips, sighs)
We’re trying to keep her away from heroin.

Kendall looks up—blank, but processing.

**KENDALL**
Excuse me?

**JIM**
It’s a struggle.  Always is.  And cocaine…

(casual shrug)
That’s a whole other battlefield.

He leans against the wall like it’s all just weather.

**JIM**
How morally flexible are you, Weatherby?

She blinks.  Doesn’t answer right away.

**JIM**
Because this isn’t policy memos and C-SPAN hearings anymore.  This is a story about **sex, drugs, and rock and roll, baby.**  Not necessarily in that order.  More like an *ice cream sundae of sin.*  And sometimes the cherry’s laced with speed.

**KENDALL** (coolly)
I worked for an administration that lied about a blowjob while ignoring Rwanda.  I think I can handle a couple unhealthy habits and some backstage orgies.

**JIM** (grins)
Good.  Because this isn’t rehab.  It’s Commuted.  And nobody’s clean here.  Not really.

He straightens, steps closer, just enough to lower his voice.

**JIM**
But if it ever gets to be too much—if you need out, or time, or armor—you come to me.  Because this storm eats people, Kendall.  And you’re too fucking good to get swallowed.

She nods.  Tight.  Focused.

**KENDALL**
I didn’t come here to get clean.  I came here to stay awake.

He raises his cup to that.

**JIM**
Then buckle up.  It’s gonna be loud.

---

## **INT.  GUND ARENA – UTILITY STAIRWELL – CONTINUED**

Kendall’s arms are folded.  She’s still holding onto the weight of Jim’s warning—but trying to parse *him*, now.  The man behind the rhythm, behind the warnings.  The man who hasn’t touched hard drugs, hasn’t cheated, hasn’t imploded—yet somehow still *fits* in this machine.

**KENDALL** (eyebrow raised)
Alright, Brown.  You’ve warned me about Kathy’s needle, Gilley’s zipper, and the band’s collective dysfunction.  What about *you?*  What’s your vice of choice?

**JIM** (grins without hesitation)
Redheads.  And barbershop quartets, baby.

Kendall blinks.

**KENDALL**
Barbershop quartets?

**JIM**
Dead serious.  Four-part harmony and a straw hat.  You ought to see my hat.

**KENDALL** (tilting her head)
So your biggest addiction is synchronized mustache music?

**JIM**
Nah.  That’s just the cover story.  The real vice?

He leans in just a little.

**JIM**
*Falling for people who know exactly who they are, and still ask questions anyway.*

Kendall narrows her eyes.  Then grins.

**KENDALL**
So basically, you like mirrors with teeth.

**JIM**
That’s my kind of gospel.

They stand there in a pause that’s not quite silence.  The stairwell hums.  Then Kendall turns toward the door.

**KENDALL**
Alright, Harmony Man.  Let’s go see if your band survives lunch.

**JIM**
Lead the way, Ms.  Weatherby.  But I’m bringing my hat next time.  Don’t say I didn’t warn you.

---

## **INT.  GUND ARENA – UTILITY STAIRWELL – CONTINUED**

They’re halfway down the steps when Kendall glances over her shoulder.

**KENDALL**
You gonna explain the hat thing?  Because barbershop quartets is weird, even for you.

**JIM** (grinning)
It’s practical.

**KENDALL**
It’s *insane.*

**JIM**
You ever stood under a dozen stage lights and then walked into a crowd of fans holding flash cameras?

**KENDALL**
Can’t say I have.

**JIM**
It’s like standing inside a fucking disco ball.  And me?  I got a head so bald, if you shine a flashlight on it, planes try to land.

**KENDALL** (stifling a laugh)
It’s not that bad.

**JIM**
Kendall—my scalp is smoother than my *ass,* and I exfoliate that with bourbon and guilt.

She actually cracks, laughing out loud.

**KENDALL**
That’s the most Jim Brown thing I’ve ever heard.

**JIM**
It’s not about fashion.  It’s about survival.  That hat is the only thing standing between me and a retina burn on the front page of *Rolling Stone.*

He gives her a wink, still grinning.

**JIM**
Besides—nothing says “I’m emotionally grounded” like four-part harmony and straw accessories.

---

## **INT.  GUND ARENA – BACKSTAGE – NEAR MAKEUP AND WARDROBE STATION – LATER**

Kendall’s standing by a rolling rack of leather jackets and torn denim, trying to make sense of a laminated “RUN OF SHOW” taped to a mirror.  Fluorescents buzz overhead.  Behind her, a camera flash pops *once*, *twice*, *again.*  She flinches.  Turns to see a roadie snapping “candid” shots of Kathy’s wardrobe table.

**JIM** sidles up beside her, sipping something caffeinated that probably isn’t.

**JIM**
You’re gonna have to learn how to wear sunglasses indoors.

**KENDALL** (flat)
Is that a drug thing?

**JIM** (smiling)
For some of us.  For some of *Rock Nation*, absolutely.

**KENDALL**
Well, I’m not high.

**JIM**
Not yet.

She gives him a look.

**JIM** (serious now)
Look—here’s the deal.  They’re going to be taking *hundreds*, maybe *thousands* of pictures a day.  Of us.  Of them.  Of the *space between.*

He gestures around at the chaos.

**JIM**
And you?  You’re in the *splash zone.*

**KENDALL**
I’m not a performer.

**JIM**
Doesn’t matter.  You’re going to be in the background.  Of shots on tour buses, at airports, backstage, red carpets, press lines, fan meetups, *you name it.*  No one will know your name.  But your face?

**He taps her lightly between the eyes.**

**JIM**
That face is gonna be in *hundreds* of pictures printed all over the world.  365 days a year.

**KENDALL** (slowly getting it)
So the glasses are…

**JIM**
Armor.  Privacy.  Consistency.  And plausible deniability.

**KENDALL**
What if I look like a narc?

**JIM**
Then you’re doing it right.  Learn how to wear sunglasses indoors.  *Learn how to wear sunglasses indoors.*

She looks at her reflection.  Then back at Jim.

**KENDALL**
Any other survival tips?

**JIM**
Yeah.  Keep your ID and your self-respect in separate pockets.  You’ll lose one eventually.

---

## **INT.  MARINE MIDLAND ARENA – TUNNEL HALLWAY – BUFFALO, NY – MARCH 1998 – NIGHT**

The snow outside is biblical.  Inside, it’s sweat and soundcheck vibrations.

**Jim** and **Kendall** walk side by side past road cases labeled “COM - BUFF NY - 03/98.” The air smells like burnt wiring and bad coffee.

**JIM**
You gotta be real careful with Jeff.

**KENDALL**
Evans?

**JIM**
Yeah.  Bass.  Soul of a sledgehammer.  Thinks Richard Nixon is the greatest American president of all time.

**KENDALL** (stops walking)
You have *got* to be shitting me.

**JIM** (shakes his head)
Not shitting.  Not even a little.  He says, five hundred years from now, the American history books will boil the whole 20th century down to one sentence:

**(in a mock gravitas voice)**
*Nixon went to China.*

**KENDALL**
Jesus.  Christ.

**JIM**
And he means it.  He can be obsessive.  And he’s probably smarter than you.

**KENDALL**
Now *you’re* shitting me.

**JIM**
Nope.  You might be faster.  You might be sharper.  But Jeff?

**(beat)**
He’s the kind of smart that **wakes up with completed essays in his head.**  There’s a reason we’ve sold twenty-five million albums.  And it’s not just because Kathy can scream and Gilley can solo like he’s on fire.  It’s because Jeff **can write better than anybody on the fucking planet.**

**KENDALL** (skeptical)
Better than me?

**JIM**
You’d have to go back two centuries and dig up some dead white guys to find a better writer.  And even then, they’d probably lose in a cage match.

**KENDALL**
So don’t underestimate him.

**JIM**
Exactly.  And for God’s sake—don’t argue politics unless you *really* want to bleed.

**KENDALL**
Got it.  Smart Nixonian bass player.  Understated genius with Cold War taste.  Totally normal ecosystem you’ve built here.

**JIM**
Welcome to the last functional band in America.

---

## **INT. MARINE MIDLAND ARENA – SERVICE ENTRANCE – BUFFALO, NY – MOMENTS LATER**

The *back door groans open* and a *blast of wind* kicks through the hallway like a ghost pissed it couldn’t get on the guest list.

Enter **JEFF EVANS**.  **Wool trench coat.  Fur-lined hat with ear flaps.  Scarf wound three times tight around his neck.  Fingerless gloves over leather gloves.** He looks like he’s been standing outside waiting for **the fall of civilization.**  **Jim** nudges **Kendall** before she even sees him.

**JIM**
Here comes the end of the world, dressed like it’s *trying to kill him.*

Jeff rounds the corner—**frost on his eyebrows**, *stoic as a gravestone*.  He’s carrying a paper cup of coffee like it personally betrayed him.

**KENDALL**  (half under her breath)
Jesus Christ, it's like summer if we were in Atlanta.

**JIM** (low)
He’s got Southern blood.  And a *deep grudge* against winter.  Says lake effect snow is a design flaw in God’s architecture.

Jeff reaches them.  Nods once.  Doesn’t smile.  Doesn’t slow down. **Keeps walking.**

**JEFF** (to no one in particular)
Buffalo can kiss both sides of my dick.

Gone.  Silence.

**KENDALL**
So… that was Jeff?

**JIM**
Yup.  That’s the man who wrote half of *Робость* in a Waffle House napkin booth while reading *Clausewitz*.

**KENDALL**
Did he just threaten the weather?

**JIM**
Every time it snows, somewhere in the back of his head, he’s planning to secede from the sky.

---

## **INT. MARINE MIDLAND ARENA – BACKSTAGE HALLWAY – MOMENTS AFTER JEFF’S ARRIVAL**

The door has long since closed.  Jeff’s snow-draped silhouette is gone down the hall.  Kendall stares after him like she’s just witnessed an unexplained natural event.

**KENDALL**
Was that…  supposed to be a greeting?

**JIM**
Yeah.

**KENDALL**
That was “hello”?

**JIM**  (laughs, nods)
Yup.  In Jeff-speak, *“Buffalo can kiss both sides of my dick”* means:  *“I see you.  I’m here.  I’m suffering.  Let’s begin.”*

**KENDALL**
Do I need a phrasebook?

**JIM**
Nah.  You just need to remember:  Jeff doesn’t do social cues.  He does *emotional thermonuclear readouts.*  If he’s talking—*even if he sounds like a rage weather report*—you’re in.

**KENDALL**
So the key is to ignore the profanity and focus on the implied civility?

**JIM**
Exactly.  If Jeff hates you?  He says nothing.  If he tolerates you?  He’ll insult your hometown, your fashion choices, and your presence *within seconds of eye contact.*

**KENDALL**
And if he *likes* me?

**JIM**
Oh, then he’ll give you a book.  No explanation.  No conversation.  Just drop it in your lap like a cat leaving a dead bird.

**KENDALL**
And I’ll be expected to read it?

**JIM**
Cover to cover.  And he’ll test you later.

Kendall exhales slowly.

**KENDALL**
Why do I feel like I just got drafted into a secret society run by angry poets?

**JIM**
Because you did.  Welcome to Commuted.

---

## **INT.  MARINE MIDLAND ARENA – CATERING LOUNGE – EVENING**

The room’s a weird hybrid: half cafeteria, half war zone.  Tables cluttered with laminated setlists, Sharpies, and half-eaten quinoa.  Roadies pass in clumps.  There’s a cheese tray that looks like it lost a fight.  **At the far end**, a man sits alone at a small table.  **No food.  No plate.  No phone.**  Just a **single glass** of **perfectly clear ice water** in front of him.  **JEFF EVANS.**  Staring at it like he’s waiting for it to confess something.

**Jim** walks up with **Kendall** in tow.

**JIM** (quietly, to Kendall)
Okay.  Context: Jeff is a snob about tap water.

**KENDALL**
You mean like, bottled vs.  tap?

**JIM**
No.  Worse.  He thinks the **mineral content** in the water from the **Great Miami Valley aquifer**, back home in southwest Ohio, is **superior to all other tap water on earth.**

**KENDALL**
He has a favorite *aquifer*?

**JIM**
He has a *doctrine.*  And because he’s a rock star now, people actually *haul jugs* of it around the country for him.  That glass?  That’s Dayton, Ohio, baby.  Vintage.

They reach the table.  Jeff doesn’t look up.  Just speaks.

**[[4.3 JEFF EVANS character bible|JEFF]]**
If this is some kind of emotional ambush, I reserve the right to throw this water on both of you.

**JIM**
Relax.  No emotions.  Just logistics.

**JEFF** (sips)
Better.

**JIM**
Jeff Evans, meet Kendall Weatherby.  She’s the new internal media lead.

**JEFF** (sips again, eyes still on the glass)
So she’s the memory now?

**KENDALL**
Only the parts that aren’t classified.

**JEFF** (eyes flick up briefly)
Good answer.

Silence.  Another sip.

**JEFF**
If you want a real introduction, you can drink from the jug.  Otherwise, just don’t move my table.

**KENDALL**
Are there notes of limestone?

**JEFF** (chuckling—barely)
She stays.

---

## **INT.  MARINE MIDLAND ARENA – CATERING LOUNGE – MINUTES LATER**

**Kendall** is seated across from **Jeff Evans**, still in front of his single glass of Dayton’s finest.  She’s got coffee.  He’s got purity.  He studies her—not like a creep, but like a man trying to decide if a file folder is misfiled.

**JEFF**
You talk a lot of game about systems.  Politics.  Memory.  So let’s pivot.

**KENDALL** (eyebrow raised)
Sure.  To what?

**JEFF**
The **Great Miami Valley Aquifer.**  In particular, I’d like to discuss the **wellhead protection scheme** employed by the City of Dayton.

Kendall blinks once.

**JEFF**
It’s the most sophisticated public-access wellhead protection program in the United States.  It predates the 1996 amendments to the Safe Drinking Water Act.  It integrates **hydrogeologic mapping**, **spill containment**, and **industrial zoning buffers**—And nobody talks about it.  Nobody knows.

**KENDALL**
Because nobody in Washington gives a damn about aquifers until there’s lead in a child’s sippy cup.

**JEFF** (grins)
Exactly.

He leans in, eyes alive now.

**JEFF**
You know what else?  Dayton treats the **entire recharge zone** as a protected territory.  Not just the immediate wellhead.  It’s proactive.  Strategic. *Elegant.*  No other city does that.  Not like this.

**KENDALL**
So you’re in a rock band because you couldn’t get a planning job in Montgomery County?

**JEFF**
I’m in a rock band because writing songs about aquifers doesn’t sell.  But that doesn’t mean I forgot how to **read an environmental impact study.**

**KENDALL**
Fair.  And you’re not wrong—Dayton’s system is impressive.  But I’d love to see how it holds up under privatization pressure or another train derailment near the Mad River.

**JEFF**
Now you’re speaking my language.

Silence.  He finally sets the glass down.

**JEFF**
Okay.  You’re smarter than they warned me.

**KENDALL**
Who’s “they”?

**JEFF**
Everyone.

---

## **INT.  MARINE MIDLAND ARENA – CATERING LOUNGE – CONTINUED**

Jeff leans forward, fingertips resting on his now half-empty glass of Dayton water like it’s a communion chalice.  Kendall has stopped writing.  She’s *listening.*

**JEFF**
So I want to understand your position on the **privatization of public water supplies.**

**KENDALL**  (domestic policy instincts kick in)
My position?  That water should be publicly held and federally protected.  Full stop.

**JEFF**
That’s American idealism.  Let’s talk *Africa*.  Let’s talk **Accra.**

**KENDALL** (surprised)
You’ve been to Ghana?

**JEFF** (tight nod)
We toured West Africa last year.  Couldn’t get a clean glass of water in Accra at *any* venue.  Not backstage, not at the hotels.  Not even from the people who were supposed to be running the treatment plants.

**(beat)**
Even the water *workers* were drinking bottled.

**KENDALL**
Because they knew the system was toxic.

**JEFF**
Exactly.  So, I got pissed.

**KENDALL**
So, what did you do—donate filters?

**JEFF**
No.  I dropped thirty million dollars into a public-private utility consortium and started **rebuilding the entire grid**.  Top to bottom.  New mains.  New tanks.  New distribution philosophy.
And now?

**(leans back, calm)**
Now we’re delivering **clear, clean, high-quality H2O** to tens of thousands.  And we’re adding **thousands more a month.**

Kendall just stares at him.

**KENDALL**
You did what?

**JEFF**
You heard me.

**KENDALL**
Privately?

**JEFF**
Publicly owned.  Privately driven.  Local governance.  Shared ownership model.  I own about 20 percent.  I’m not building a bottling empire.  I’m building dignity.  With *plumbing.*

**KENDALL**
Why Accra?

**JEFF**
Because someone had to start.  And I was tired of writing songs no one listens to about bodies in rivers.  Now I fix the water.  Let the music catch up.

**(beat)**
So… where do you stand?

Kendall doesn’t answer right away.

**KENDALL**
I stand with you.  But don’t expect that to stop me from auditing the hell out of your pipeline data.

**JEFF** (grinning faintly)
That’s all I ever wanted.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – BUFFALO, NY – THAT NIGHT**

**Kendall** is barefoot, still in her show clothes, hunched over the desk in her room.  The TV’s on mute.  The minibar’s open.  Her laptop glows with the **Alta Vista search results she didn’t expect to find.**  Her fingers hover over the keyboard.  She scrolls.  Clicks.  Scrolls again.

**JEFF EVANS \+ GHANA \+ ACCRA WATER REDEVELOPMENT**

**Page after page.**  **News snippets.  NGO blurbs.  Engineering briefs.**  There’s even a grainy photo of Jeff standing next to a cistern with a group of city officials and a banner that says: *“CLEAN FLOW.  CLEAN FUTURE.”*

She reads a sentence aloud:

**KENDALL**
“…led by private American philanthropist and musician Jeff Evans, whose donation underwrote Phase One of the new municipal water framework…”

She blinks.  Scrolls faster.  A PDF download from *The Accra Water Partnership*.  She opens it.  His name is on the letterhead. *As project director.*

**KENDALL**
Oh.  My.  *God.*

She leans back, stunned.  Stares at the ceiling.

**KENDALL**
He was telling the fucking truth.

She covers her face with both hands.

**KENDALL**
Goddamn.  Last time I was this shocked, it involved a sink, a blender, and a bottle of Absolut Citron in my parents’ kitchen.

She drops her hands, exhales slow.  Then looks at the screen again.

**KENDALL**
Okay, Evans.  You’re not full of shit.  You’re just… *a problem set I didn’t study for.*

---

## **INT.  MARINE MIDLAND ARENA – SIDE STAGE TECH ROOM – NEXT MORNING**

Wires, amps, cases—early show quiet.  No roadies yet.  Just **Jeff**, sitting on a folding chair tuning a bass that looks older than most democracies.  **Kendall** enters, fresh coffee in hand.  Calm.  Controlled.

**KENDALL**
I looked you up on the world wide web.

Jeff doesn’t look up.

**JEFF**
Yeah.  I figured.

**KENDALL**
Read all about Accra.  Clean Flow.  Municipal frameworks.  Water purity metrics that would make Los Angeles cry.

Jeff still doesn’t look up.  Adjusts a knob.

**KENDALL**
You weren’t lying.

**JEFF**
I never do.  It’s a waste of breath.

Beat.

He plucks a low E.  It hums deep, like an engine waking up.  Then he looks up.  Eyes cool, unreadable.

**JEFF**
*“Kendall Weatherby plus DC plus Vice President Gore”*—plus “reinventing government,” “policy streamlining,” “staff memo scandals,”  and a whole bunch more search strings told me a *lot* more about *you*, I bet.

**KENDALL** (steady)
Yeah?

**JEFF** (soft grin)
You had an ex-boss who was a fuckin’ dickhead.  And a resume that scared most of the Hill.  They called you the “quiet fire.”

**KENDALL**
Was that before or after Tipper told people I was trying to radicalize the interns?

**JEFF** (sips water)
Didn’t matter.  You were right either way.

Silence.  Respect thick in the air.

**KENDALL**
So what now?  We’re both busted idealists with search history?

**JEFF**
Nah.  We’re in a band.  Keep your eyes open, and don’t trust any coffee that’s already been poured.

He stands.  Picks up his bass.  Walks off.

**KENDALL** (to herself)
Yeah.  I’m gonna like you, you bastard.

---

## **INT.  CIVIC ARENA – BACKSTAGE HALLWAY – PITTSBURGH, PA – EVENING**

It’s loud.  Always is.  Crew dragging cables, someone yelling about reverb, a smell of onions and road sweat in the air.  **Kendall** ducks out of a logistics chat with the tour manager.  She’s trying to find five seconds to breathe when **Jeff** appears.  He says nothing.  Just walks up and **drops a book into her hands**.

**Marshall McLuhan – *Understanding Media: The Extensions of Man***

**KENDALL** (reading the cover)
You think I’m media, or extended man?

**JEFF**
Both.  That’s why it’ll hurt.

**KENDALL**
No note?

**JEFF**
The book *is* the note.

She flips it open—already marked, underlined in pencil, probably read a dozen times.

**KENDALL**
You really do this for everyone?

**JEFF**
Only people who might be dangerous.

She cocks an eyebrow, smiling slightly.

**JEFF**
Also, fair warning—*beware of the city.*

**KENDALL**
Why?  Smog?  Riot cops?  Surprise electoral swings?

**JEFF**
No.  They put *coleslaw on their sandwiches.*  Without asking.

He’s already walking away.

**JEFF** (half-calling back)
You take one bite, your whole brain resets.  Careful out there.

**KENDALL** (sotto)
Marshall McLuhan and sandwich terrorism.  I have never met anyone like this.

She tucks the book under her arm like it’s an assignment.  Because it is.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – PITTSBURGH, PA – LATE NIGHT**

The city outside is dark and humming.  Inside: a hotel room desk, scattered with **yellow mustard-stained napkins**, an **empty Primanti Brothers sandwich wrapper**, and an open copy of *Understanding Media* under the lamplight.  **Kendall** is sitting cross-legged in the desk chair, still chewing the final bite of **what might be the best sandwich of her life**—bread, meat, cheese, **fries**, and yes, **coleslaw**, all smashed into one glorious carb-bomb.  She swallows, licks her fingers, and looks down at the book.  Two chapters in, and already her head’s throbbing like she’s been slapped with a philosophy hammer.

**KENDALL** (reading aloud, softly)
*“The medium is the message.”*  What the hell does that even mean?

She flips back a page.  Rereads.  Eyes narrow.

**KENDALL**
Is this about me?  About the newsletter?  About *how* I write it?  Or what I choose not to say?

She leans back.  Stares at the ceiling.

**KENDALL** (to herself)
Is *everything* a test with this guy?

Beat.

She glances over at the sandwich wrapper.

**KENDALL**
The sandwich was a test.  Of course it was.  Coleslaw as metaphor.  Consumption as transformation.  Jesus Christ.

She looks back at the book.  Then out the window at Pittsburgh’s skeletal skyline.

**KENDALL**
Okay, Jeff Evans.  You want a test?  Let’s go.

She pulls her notebook closer, opens a fresh page.  **At the top, she writes:**

**“The Medium is the Myth: Commuted, Constructed Memory, and the Art of Not Looking Away.”**

Then, she starts typing.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – PITTSBURGH – 3:02 A.M.**

The room is lit only by the glow of her **laptop screen** and the green standby light on the TV she hasn’t turned on in two days.  **Kendall** sits on the edge of the bed, one shoe off, the other somewhere under the desk.  Her fingers hover above the keys.  She rereads the final paragraph of her piece.

**Title: “The Medium is the Myth”**
**Subject**: Commuted’s self-narrative, refracted through chaos, performance, and controlled fire.

It’s **tight.  Thoughtful.  Slightly dangerous.** The kind of thing you write when you’re not sure if it’ll get you hired or flagged.  She saves the draft.  Sits back.  Rubs her eyes.  Then speaks—just to the room.  Just to herself.

**KENDALL**
Alright, Cremeans.  There it is.

She exhales.

**KENDALL**
Now comes the real question—do you even want me?  Or am I just another satellite in a band that only remembers the center of gravity when they crash into something?

She stares at the wall.

**KENDALL**
Did you sit down with Kathy?  Did you sit down with *Jeff*?  Hell, have you even found **Bill** long enough to ask him anything?

She snorts.

**KENDALL**
Bill.  Mister Producer-slash-keyboard-demigod, who’s somehow still working on other people’s albums in the middle of this circus.  Guy probably sleeps in a keyboard case.

Her eyes drift toward the window.

**KENDALL**
Chicago.  Cleveland.  Buffalo.  Pittsburgh.  Jesus Christ, it’s a Rust Belt blur.

She picks up her phone.  Checks the band’s master schedule.

**KENDALL**
I think we’re headed to Philadelphia next?

(beat)

Maybe?

(sigh)
Who’s tracking?

She saves the file one more time.  Then, with the kind of casual finality only exhaustion can grant, she sends it:

**TO: Jeff Cremeans**
**SUBJECT: Submission – Kendall Weatherby Assignment #1**
**BODY:** Attached.  Title: *The Medium is the Myth*.  All quotes verified.  All barbs intentional.
Regards,
K.W.

She closes the laptop.  Leans back on the bed.

**KENDALL**
Well.  Now we wait.

And for the first time in weeks—she lets herself sleep.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – SAME NIGHT – 3:04 A.M.**

**Kendall** is lying back, barely two minutes into pretending she’s asleep when her laptop *dings*.  She sits up, blinks, opens the lid.

**EMAIL INBOX**
**FROM:** Jeff.Cremeans@commutedmedia.net
**SUBJECT:** Re: Submission – Kendall Weatherby Assignment #1

She clicks it.

**EMAIL BODY:**
**Kendall,**

Read it.  Twice.

You’ve got voice, timing, teeth.  A little heavy on the existential framing, but that’s probably what we need.  Meet me for coffee in the lobby before we load buses. 6:45 sharp.  Let’s take your temperature.  See if you’re breathing with the tour or just reporting on it.  Yes—destination is **Philadelphia.** Pack for bipolar weather and a crew that’s losing patience with itself.

—JLC

**KENDALL** (reading aloud, dry)
“Take your temperature.”  Translation: *Are you gonna break, or are you about to become essential?*

She closes the laptop again.  No smile.  Just alertness.  She checks the clock.

**3:05 A.M.**

**KENDALL**
Three hours of sleep and a possibly career-defining coffee.  Sounds about right.

She tosses the rest of her Primanti Brothers wrapper into the trash and pulls her boots closer.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL LOBBY – PITTSBURGH – 6:45 A.M.**

Dim lighting.  Quiet hum of refrigerated pastries.  A few bleary-eyed crew slouched in chairs, scrolling phones.  At a corner table, **Jeff Cremeans** sits with a **black coffee** that looks like it could strip paint.  He’s reading the news on a legal pad because he doesn’t trust screens before noon.  **Kendall** arrives, to-go cup in hand—**oat milk latte**, double shot, half sleeve.

**CREMEANS** (looking at the cup, not her)
Jesus Christ.  You’re one of *those*.

**KENDALL**
Morning.

**CREMEANS**
You know what’s wrong with oat milk?

**KENDALL**
That it makes you feel emasculated?

**CREMEANS**
That it’s *not freaking milk.*

He takes a brutal sip of his coffee like it owes him rent.  Then gestures for her to sit.  She does.

Beat.

**CREMEANS**
So.  What’ve you learned?

**KENDALL**
This is a machine held together by sex, caffeine, and three nearly-unsolvable personality disorders.  Also, the bassist is possibly operating on a god complex wrapped in deepwater municipal policy.

**CREMEANS**
Not bad.  Anything else?

**KENDALL**
Kathy’s a volcano.  Gilley’s a predator with boundaries.  Bill’s never in the room.  Jim’s smarter than he lets on.
And you?

**CREMEANS** (bracing)
Yeah?

**KENDALL**
You’re running triage while pretending it’s accounting.

Cremeans stares at her.  Then sips.  Nods—barely.

**CREMEANS**
Your writing’s *marginally* acceptable.  Minimum viable product.

**KENDALL**
Flattered.

**CREMEANS**
You play with rhythm.  You understand voice.  You’re not afraid of a little bite.  But that piece?  It was safe.  Clever, sure—but you didn’t bleed on the page.

**KENDALL**
Maybe I’m saving that for week two.

He snorts.

**CREMEANS**
Fair enough.

Beat.

**CREMEANS**
So.  Have you decided?  You staying?

She doesn’t answer right away.  Then:

**KENDALL**
You read what I wrote.  You already know I’m not leaving.

He finishes his coffee like that answer satisfied more than he’ll admit.

**CREMEANS**
Good.  Then get on the bus.

---

## **INT.  TOUR BUS – PENNSYLVANIA TURNPIKE – MIDDAY**

The bus hums.  Curtains drawn, guitars rattling softly in overhead bins.  Someone’s asleep under a blanket on the back lounge couch.  A half-played movie flickers silently on the little TV up front.  **Kendall** sits mid-bus with **Jeff Cremeans**, coffee #2 of the day in hand, iPad open, *not* reading it.  Just watching her.

**CREMEANS**
Alright.  Let’s walk through it.

**KENDALL**
Which part?

**CREMEANS**
The *part where you think you’re in.*  You’re not in the circle of trust yet.  You’ve been tolerated, vetted, mildly respected.  That’s different than trusted.

**KENDALL**
So what gets me in?

**CREMEANS**
Conversations.  Real ones.

He ticks them off on his fingers.

**CREMEANS**
You need to talk to **Bill**.  Not just pass him in hallways.  He’s holding more narrative than anyone on this bus—because he’s got *nothing left to prove.*  You need to talk to **Jeremy**—prince of melodies.  If he decides you’re ornamental, you’re screwed.  And you need to figure out what the hell you’re doing about **Gilley**.

**KENDALL**
I shut him down.

**CREMEANS**
You shut him down once.  But if there’s *any* daylight left in your signals, he’ll squeeze through.  Be smart, Kendall.  He respects clear boundaries.  Not “maybe someday” vibes.

She exhales.  Nods.

**CREMEANS**
And then we’ve got **Kathy** and **Jeff**.  Neither trust you.  Yet.  Because you haven’t dug in with them.  Haven’t **shown up** where it counts.

**KENDALL**
I wrote the piece.

**CREMEANS**
You *observed*.  That’s step one.  They’re waiting for step two: *Engagement.*  Push back.  Ask something dangerous.  Bring fire to the table.  Right now, you’re *recording the riot.* They want to know if you can survive it.

She’s listening now.  Leaning in.  And then Cremeans shifts tone.  More personal.  More pointed.

**CREMEANS**
Last thing.  And this is where I stop being your editor and start being the guy who keeps the band from imploding:

**(beat)**
*What are your intentions toward my drummer?*

She blinks.

**KENDALL**
Excuse me?

**CREMEANS**
Don’t play dumb.  You’re a grown woman.  He’s a grown man.  And history already happened.  So I’m asking now, before it gets messy again—are you writing this band, or are you falling back into his bunk?

Silence.

**KENDALL**
I don’t know yet.

**CREMEANS**
Then figure it out fast.

**(beat)**
Because if you’re not sure which one it is, we’re all gonna pay for it later.

The bus rolls on.  The turnpike stretches ahead like a test.

---

## **INT.  TOUR BUS – PENNSYLVANIA TURNPIKE – LATER**

The rhythm of the road is hypnotic—*tires thumping seams, chassis creaking slightly with every curve*.  **Cremeans** is slumped back, earbuds in, *reading something that looks like SEC filings for chaos*.  He’s officially shut off.  Up front, **Tom the driver** is muttering to himself about brake pads and Pennsylvania tolls.  Kendall isn’t even sure if he’s talking to her or not.  She hopes not.  So she opens her notebook.  And begins to write.

**KENDALL’S JOURNAL – MARCH 1998 – SOMEWHERE BETWEEN PITTSBURGH AND PHILLY**

Circle of trust: still outside.  Cremeans wants me to “engage.”  Not report.  Not document.  Not observe.  **Engage.**

With Bill—who slips through cities like a rumor.
With Jeremy—who runs this entire tour like a benevolent dictatorship run on Red Bull and socket wrenches.
With Gilley—who needs a warning label tattooed on his abs.
With Kathy and Jeff—who each seem to be running internal revolutions under their skin and expect me to pick a side *without* reading the constitution first.

And then there’s Jim.

My drummer.  My ex-mistake?  Ex-moment?  Ex-sanity check?

Cremeans asked the question like it was legal deposition: *What are your intentions toward my drummer?*

I wanted to snap back, “None.”  I wanted to lie.  But I didn’t.  Because that’s how real problems start—when you pretend you’re not already drifting.  So, let me try the truth:  I don’t want to fall for him again.  But I don’t want to stay away either.  I don’t know what I want.  I just know I’m not done *watching him breathe.*  And I think that’s where the trouble lives.

She closes the notebook.  Tucks it under her thigh.  And stares out the window at gray trees flickering past like unfinished sentences.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – BACKSTAGE WIFI LOUNGE – PHILADELPHIA – LATE MORNING**

A flickering CRT monitor hums faintly in the corner of a temporary media pit set up with two folding chairs and a coffee pot that smells like gasoline.  **Kendall**, alone for a moment, does what she hasn’t done in weeks: She types in a familiar URL.  A holdover from her old life. **The kind of site that refreshes faster than press briefings can cover the damage.**

**DRUDGEREPORT.COM**

It loads byte by byte.  And there it is.

**A flashing red GIF of a police siren.  Bold text:**

**BREAKING: PRESIDENT INVOKES EXECUTIVE PRIVILEGE TO BLOCK GRAND JURY TESTIMONY**

**KENDALL** (softly, flatly)
Oh, fuck me.

She scrolls.  Headlines rush past:

- *"WH Counsel Signals Stonewall Tactic"*
- *"Immunity Talks Deadlocked"*
- *"Independent Counsel Reportedly Furious"*

She stops breathing for a moment.  Then leans back in the chair like she’s just been slapped.  She whispers to herself.  The kind of whisper that could strip paint.

**KENDALL**
You don’t invoke executive privilege unless you’re hiding something.  You don’t wrap yourself in the Constitution unless your suit is bleeding.

Her face goes red.  Not embarrassed—*furious.*  She remembers every *briefing*, every *bullshit talking point*, every **memo she was forced to help craft to spin this man as morally complex rather than plainly corrupt.**

**KENDALL**
You.  Fucking.  Liar.

She closes the site, slams the monitor off.  Stands.  Paces.  She grips the back of a folding chair like it might run away if she lets go.

**KENDALL**
You made me defend you.  You made me defend *rape.*

She swipes her tour badge off the table.  Clips it back to her belt with a sharp SNAP.

**KENDALL**
Never again.

She steps out of the lounge and back into the backstage madness—*but this time*, her fire isn’t coming from backstage chaos.  It’s coming from the truth.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – CATERING ROOM – MIDDAY – MARCH 20, 1998**

The smell of coffee, hot lights, stale backstage bagels.  Crew are chattering.  Someone’s tuning a guitar in the distance.  Kendall sits alone at a table with her **notebook open**, eyes burning with the kind of clarity that only comes when **you’ve had enough lies to last a lifetime**.  She’s not shaking.  She’s not blinking.  She’s *resolute*.  She writes.  Fast.  Sharp.  No crossings out.

**KENDALL’S NOTEBOOK – MARCH 20, 1998 – PHILADELPHIA**

I know now why the scandal in D.C.  is going to **implode**.  It’s not the sex.  It’s not the ego.  It’s not even the abuse of power.  It’s the **lie.**  If they’d told the truth from the start, unflinchingly, the whole damn thing—it would’ve been a **one-day story**.  Forgotten by the weekend.  But instead, they stacked lies like sandbags, and now the whole levee’s going to break.

So here’s my doctrine:  If I’m going to write for this band—if I’m going to *build this media department from scratch*—Then I’m going to tell the **truth.**  The whole truth.  Nothing but the truth.  **Unflinchingly.  Unstintingly.  Unsparingly.**  If I’m the eyes and ears of this band?  Then *they’d better be ready to be seen.*  And if we’re going to put out **17,000 newsletters a month**, then by God—**they’re going to be worth reading.**

She tears the page from the notebook.  Pins it to the inside flap of her work binder.  Her gospel.  Then she stands.  Because it’s time to write like people’s *myths* depend on it.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – STAGE LEFT CORRIDOR – MID-AFTERNOON**

Kendall is moving fast.  Notebook in hand.  On fire from her decision, charged up, ready to corner someone—maybe Kathy, maybe Jeff—**anyone to unload her new clarity onto.**  Then she turns the corner and nearly walks *smack* into—**BILL DAVENPORT.**

And she *freezes*.  Because **Bill**—keyboardist, producer, occasional wizard of chaos—looks like he’s **escaped the '80s via military enlistment**.  Gone is the shoulder-length,  poofed-out, glam-metal legacy hair.

In its place?  **A precise, clean, tight-ass crew cut.**

**KENDALL** (eyes wide)
*What the hell, Bill?*

He looks up, grinning like nothing’s happened.

**BILL**
Afternoon, Weatherby.

**KENDALL**
Did… did you lose a bet?  Get court-martialed?  Join the Marine Corps tribute band?

**BILL**
Nah.

**(deadpan)**
Got tired of getting conditioner in my synth rig.

She blinks.  Still staring.

**KENDALL**
You cut your hair.

**BILL**
Yup.

**KENDALL**
You—*you had hair like a poodle that got electrocuted during a Poison show, and now you’re walking around like you do IT for the Department of Transportation?*

**BILL** (smiling)
*Finally*, someone says it out loud.

She circles him once, like she’s not sure it’s actually him.

**KENDALL**
Why?

**BILL**
I turned twenty-eight and realized the only thing louder than my solos was the silence when I walked into rooms looking like a time capsule.  So I changed the hair.  The music stayed the same.

**KENDALL**
You’re a keyboardist in a rock band, Bill.  You’re *supposed* to look like an electrical accident.

**BILL** (taps his temple)
Evolution, baby.

**(beat)**
Besides—felt like time to stop looking like the past.

**KENDALL** (stares a beat longer)
Jesus.  I can’t even roast you for that.  That’s… actually profound.

**BILL**
Don’t get used to it.  Next week I might grow a mustache.

He walks off.  Kendall just watches him go.

**KENDALL** (to herself)
Crew cut.  Jesus Christ.  What the *hell* is in the water on this tour?

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – TUNNEL STAIRWELL – LATER THAT AFTERNOON**

A concrete stairwell halfway between nowhere and greenroom.  Quiet.  Echoey.  Smells like floor polish and old tour posters.  **Bill** is sitting on the second step from the bottom, sipping green tea like it’s whiskey.  His crew cut somehow makes him look younger and weirder.  **Kendall** slides down the wall beside him, notebook clutched but unopened.  There’s a long pause.  Not awkward.  Just… hanging.

**KENDALL**
I’ve got, like, a hundred questions.

**BILL**
You always lead with that or just when the caffeine spikes?

**KENDALL**
This time it’s post-rage spiral.  D.C.  stuff.

**BILL**
Ah.  Political trauma.  We’ve all got our poison.

**KENDALL**
Okay.  Let’s start weird and work backwards.

He gestures: go for it.

**KENDALL**
Where were you born?

**BILL**
Marion, Indiana.  Where dreams go to die or become basketball metaphors.

**KENDALL**
Did you have a sister?

**BILL**
Still do.  Shannon.  Hairdresser.  Hates my music.  Loves my bank account.

**KENDALL**
Favorite form of potato?

**BILL**
Tater tots.  Fight me.

**KENDALL** (rapid-fire)
What’s your favorite chord?  What’s the most overrated synth brand?  Do you think the Beatles were better high or sober?

**BILL**
D minor.  Anything labeled “vintage” and priced like a Vespa.  And the Beatles weren’t better—they were just braver when they were high.

**KENDALL** (amused, nervous)
My god, am I botching this?

**BILL** (smiles faintly)
A little.  But it’s charming.  You’re like a caffeinated anthropologist in a war zone.

**KENDALL**
I’m just trying to figure out who’s real before I start writing about ghosts.

**BILL**
That’s a good line.

**KENDALL**
Thanks.  I think I stole it from someone better than me.

**BILL**
All the good writers do.

She finally opens her notebook.

**KENDALL**
You mind if I document this?

**BILL**
Only if you spell “tater tot” right.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – STAIRWELL – SAME CONVERSATION, CONTINUED**

Kendall has the notebook balanced on her knee now, pen poised, finally settled into a rhythm.  She looks over at Bill, tone shifting just slightly—genuine curiosity under her dry edge.

**KENDALL**
How long have you known Jeff?

**BILL** (pauses, thinking)
Jesus.  Since we were sixteen?  We met in a music theory class that was half acidheads and half overachievers.  He was both.

**KENDALL**
Has he ever given you a copy of *Marshall McLuhan*?

Bill bursts out laughing.  Not a chuckle—**a full, manic, can't-catch-his-breath cackle** that echoes up the stairwell.

**BILL**
Oh my *God*.  You got one of those?

**KENDALL** (chuckling, confused)
Is this a thing?

**BILL**
Yeah, it’s a thing.  That’s the **Jeff Evans litmus test.**  He only gives McLuhan to people he doesn’t hate.

**KENDALL**
So it’s… what?  An honor?

**BILL**
No.  It’s a *challenge.*  He’s watching now to see if you quote it in conversation or if you internalize it without turning into a pretentious wreck.

**KENDALL**
I’ve only read two chapters.

**BILL**
Then he’s waiting.

**KENDALL**
For what?

**BILL**
For the moment you either understand what he’s trying to say—or you throw it in a trash can and tell him to write his own damn media theory.

**(beat)**
Either way, that’s when he starts respecting you.

She leans her head back against the wall.

**KENDALL**
I feel like I joined a cult and no one handed me the rules.

**BILL**
Welcome to Commuted.  Our robes are made of denim and bad decisions.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – STAIRWELL – SAME CONVERSATION**

Kendall’s notebook is open, her pen idle now.  She’s not writing anymore.  She’s just *listening.*

**BILL**
You know… we’ve been on the road basically nonstop for **seven years**.

**KENDALL**
Jesus.

**BILL**
Yeah.  Seven years of *buses and basements and bunkers with lights*.  We changed our setlists.  Changed our clothes.  Changed *cities* three times a week.  And we changed the music, too.

He pauses.  Fingers tapping the rim of his tea cup.

**BILL**
We started out a **synth band.**  Hardcore ‘80s pulse.  Electric, theatrical.  Almost new wave with attitude.  Then we got caught in the grunge undertow—touched it, bounced off it.  Didn’t quite fit, didn’t quite fake it.

**KENDALL**
So what are you now?

**BILL**
*Inventive.*  We take sounds we like and break them until they feel like ours.

**(beat)**
We’ve rewritten the songbook once.  We’ll probably do it again.

**KENDALL**
Because of pressure?

**BILL**
Because we get bored.  And because we’re trying to do two things at the same time.

**KENDALL**
Which are?

**BILL**
*Change the world.*  And *leave it exactly the same.*

She looks at him.

**KENDALL**
That’s contradictory.

**BILL**
Exactly.  That’s the tension.  That’s the band.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – STAIRWELL – LATE AFTERNOON**

The air’s gone still in the way only concrete backstage air can—*dead, stale, private*.  Kendall is still seated next to Bill.  Her notebook’s in her lap, but she hasn’t written anything in a minute.  She looks over at him.  Quietly.

**KENDALL**
Bill…Is Jeff that crazy?

Bill doesn’t flinch.  Doesn’t laugh.  He just lets the question hang for a second.  Then:

**BILL**
Jim once mocked him in a garage.

**KENDALL**
Okay?

**BILL**
This was *years* ago.  Back when we were just starting—cheap amps, unpaid gigs, sweat and duct tape.  Jeff had just come off a real… *Jeff episode*.  You’ll know one when you see it.
Jim made a joke about it.  Kinda offhand, kinda mean.

**(beat)**
And Jeremy—Jeff’s brother—got right up in his face and said he’d kick his ass if he *ever* talked about Jeff like that again.

**KENDALL**
Jesus.  Jim?

**BILL**
Yup.

**KENDALL**
Jim could probably snap Jeremy in half.

**BILL**
Maybe.  But the smart money was on Jeremy.  Because he was **completely livid** and **completely fearless**.  Didn’t matter if he lost the fight.  He was going to *make a point.*

**(beat)**
That’s what it means to be near Jeff.  Nobody fully understands him.  Nobody’s ever going to.  Not even his wife.  Especially not his wife.

**KENDALL**
So why even try?

**BILL**
Because sometimes…he writes something that sounds like it was channeled from a place *before language*.  Because sometimes he says things that unlock your *bones* even if they don’t make sense.

He shrugs.

**BILL**
He won’t make sense for a year or two.  He’s not built to.  He does this—*the riddles, the side glances, the McLuhan drops*—because it’s how he survives people.  He finds it **hard to relate.**
So until he’s comfortable, *you just get samples*.

**KENDALL**
Samples?

**BILL**
Yeah.  Glimpses.  Snippets.  Like he’s testing the world for interference before he plugs in fully.

She’s silent a moment.

**KENDALL**
How do you know when he’s fully plugged in?

**BILL**
You won’t.  But when it happens, you’ll feel like the air in the room just learned how to talk.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – STAIRWELL – MOMENTS LATER**

Kendall’s legs are crossed now, notebook on the floor, eyes locked on Bill like she’s trying to figure out how the hell this band hasn’t been dissected by grad students yet.  She leans forward.

**KENDALL**
Okay.  Real question.

**BILL**
Hit me.

**KENDALL**
How the *fuck* does Jeff write like that?

**BILL** (grins)
Like what?

**KENDALL**
Like he understands *everything*.  Sex, rage, grief, womanhood, queerness—*intimacy without shame*.  And he doesn’t even talk in straight lines.

**(beat)**
I’ve read the lyrics.  Half of them are **uncomfortably good**.  Better than most of the Hill speechwriters I worked with.  So how?  How does he *do* that?

Bill stretches his back against the cold wall.  Cracks his knuckles.

**BILL**
He does *pretty good on paper*.  But that’s the trick—he’s not the voice.  He gives his words to *other people*—to **Kathy**, to **Gilley**, even to **me**, sometimes.  He doesn’t deliver them.  He *distills* them.

**KENDALL**
So he’s the ghostwriter of your soul?

**BILL**
Sometimes.  But here’s the second trick—he’s not doing it alone.

**(leans forward)**
We have a **collective writing establishment.**  It’s chaos, but it’s also chemistry.  He drafts.  I rearrange.  Gilley tears it apart and tries to make it sexier.  Kathy shaves it down to the bone.

**(smiling)**
Some of us act like *sandpaper*.  Try to wear down his rough edges, **round off the math**, bring in more blood.

**KENDALL**
Jesus.  You’re a collaborative brain trust with a feedback loop from hell.

**BILL**
Exactly.

**(beat)**
The lyrics sound like he knows you because they’re *edited by people who do*.  He reaches into the abstract.  We drag it back down to the skin.

Kendall sits with that.  Eyes narrowing.

**KENDALL**
You’re saying it’s a machine.

**BILL**
No.  I’m saying it’s a **ritual.**

---
## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – STAIRWELL – SAME CONVERSATION**

Bill’s tone shifts now.  Less casual.  More deliberate.  This is **history** he’s handing over—and **warning** in equal measure.

**BILL**
You ever looked at the liner notes for a Beatles album?

**KENDALL**
Yeah.  Obsessively.

**BILL**
Good.  Next time you’re near a Tower Records, grab one again.  Then pick up a copy of ours—***69 Reasons***.

**KENDALL**
Already on my list.

**BILL**
Look close.  Every single track?  Written by **Commuted**.

**(leans in slightly)**
That’s all it ever says.

**KENDALL**
Collective authorship.

**BILL**
Exactly.  That’s the surface.  But underneath?  I can tell you because I was *there*.  **Come Inside Me.  Track 21.**  The one we use to close every city, no matter what.  That one?

**(softly)**
Half Jeff.  Half Kathy.  But I’ll never tell you which half is which.

**KENDALL**
Why?

**BILL**
Because that’s part of the game.

**(grinning now)**
We *want* the media to chase shadows.  Jeff’ll say in Bangkok: *“I wrote the chorus.”*  Then in Kuala Lumpur, Kathy’ll say: *“No, I did.  Jeff just added the bridge.”*  And then Gilley?  When we hit Singapore?

**(laughs)**
He’ll contradict *both* of them.  Just to fuck with everyone.

**KENDALL**
So it’s misinformation by design?

**BILL**
No—*it’s art as a decoy*.  We write it, sing it, break it, rebuild it.  But we never hand you the full blueprint.

**(beat)**
You need to understand, Kendall: Everyone in this band is an **unreliable narrator**.

**KENDALL**
Even you?

**BILL**
Especially me.
## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – STAIRWELL – SAME CONVERSATION**

Bill’s tone shifts now.  Less casual.  More deliberate.  This is **history** he’s handing over—and **warning** in equal measure.

**BILL**
You ever looked at the liner notes for a Beatles album?

**KENDALL**
Yeah.  Obsessively.

**BILL**
Good.  Next time you’re near a Tower Records, grab one again.  Then pick up a copy of ours—***69 Reasons***.

**KENDALL**
Already on my list.

**BILL**
Look close.  Every single track?  Written by **Commuted**.

**(leans in slightly)**
That’s all it ever says.

**KENDALL**
Collective authorship.

**BILL**
Exactly.  That’s the surface.  But underneath?  I can tell you because I was *there*.  **Come Inside Me.  Track 21.**  The one we use to close every city, no matter what.  That one?

**(softly)**
Half Jeff.  Half Kathy.  But I’ll never tell you which half is which.

**KENDALL**
Why?

**BILL**
Because that’s part of the game.

**(grinning now)**
We *want* the media to chase shadows.  Jeff’ll say in Bangkok: *“I wrote the chorus.”*  Then in Kuala Lumpur, Kathy’ll say: *“No, I did.  Jeff just added the bridge.”*  And then Gilley?  When we hit Singapore?

**(laughs)**
He’ll contradict *both* of them.  Just to fuck with everyone.

**KENDALL**
So it’s misinformation by design?

**BILL**
No—*it’s art as a decoy*.  We write it, sing it, break it, rebuild it.  But we never hand you the full blueprint.

**(beat)**
You need to understand, Kendall: Everyone in this band is an **unreliable narrator**.

**KENDALL**
Even you?

**BILL**
Especially me.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – STAIRWELL – SAME CONVERSATION, CONTINUED**

Kendall leans forward, voice tight.  Not angry. *Just overwhelmed.*

**KENDALL**
How do I do my job, Bill?

**BILL** (softly)
You’ve got *two* jobs.

She blinks.

**BILL**
You just haven’t figured it out yet.

**(beat)**
First job?  Tell the truth.  To the fans.  To the people who keep showing up.  To the ones who’ve listened through breakups, lineups, hospital visits, and the fire that happened in Tucson—*and still come back.*

**KENDALL**
And the second?

**BILL**
Figure out how to **stay employed.**

**(beat)**
Because if you tell the truth *too often,* someone’s going to come headhunting.  Might be Kathy.  Might be Jeff.  Might be Cremeans with a clipboard and a soft suggestion you “recalibrate your editorial tone.”

**(shrugs)**
But that’s the dance.  You tell enough truth to matter.  Not so much that it costs us the illusion.

She exhales.  Then starts to nod—slow, resigned.  But Bill holds up a finger.

**BILL**
Actually…You’ve got a *third* job.

**KENDALL** (sighs)
Of course I do.

**BILL**
You’re the **archivist**.  You’re the one who’s supposed to remember what the rest of us forget.  Not the headlines.  Not the setlists.  The *real shit*.

**(leans back)**
Like… what *were* they serving at the craft table when we were in Cleveland?

Kendall blinks.

**KENDALL**
I—

(pause)
Was it those terrible wraps with the green tortilla?

**BILL**
No, that was Buffalo.    Cleveland had the weird peanut butter hummus.  Gilley threw it at a light tech.

**KENDALL**
Jesus Christ.

**BILL**
Exactly.  That’s your job too.  **Be the memory.**

**(softly)**
Because one day we’re going to forget *everything,* and you’re the only one writing it down.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – MERCH STORAGE ROOM – EVENING**

Kendall stands alone between crates of t-shirts and unopened boxes of tour stickers, lit only by the soft yellow glow of a hanging bulb.  She’s holding her notebook open.  Two columns.

**Left Side Header:**
*ARCHIVE – PUBLIC*

**Right Side Header:**
*ARCHIVE – PRIVATE*

She’s already begun listing:

- **Cleveland, March 17**
  *Public:* “Solid show, minor tech hiccup, huge encore energy.”
  *Private:* “Gilley launched a hummus container at the lighting rig.  Jeff didn’t flinch.”

- **Buffalo, March 19**
  *Public:* “Intimate energy, Bill debuted new bridge riff.”
  *Private:* “Kathy refused to speak backstage.  Was crying during soundcheck.  Still nailed the show.”

She stops and stares at the two columns.  Smirks.  Then laughs—*quiet, real laughter*.

**KENDALL** (to herself)
Of course there are two archives.  Because this is Commuted.  A band with **one name, six versions of the truth.**

She steps back, closes the notebook.  Feels it now—not just as a task, but as a **rite of belonging**.

**KENDALL**
This is the job.  Keep both stories alive.  One for the world, one for the family.

**(beat)**
And hate it.  But do it well.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – PHILADELPHIA – NIGHT BEFORE THE SHOW**

Kendall’s pacing.  Notebook open.  Pen in hand.  Hair a mess.  Her fourth coffee of the day is vibrating on the nightstand.  She’s muttering to herself.

**KENDALL**
Okay.  Okay.  Two people—two *quite different* people—have told me the same thing: *engage with Kathy*.  And don’t do it wrong.

She paces faster.

**KENDALL**
What does that even *mean*?  Don’t be fake.  Don’t be afraid.  Don’t try to out-alpha her, don’t act like you’ve read her whole trauma arc.

**(beat)**
So how do I not make her hate me?

She stops.  Breathes.  Then the realization hits: **just go.  Just fire questions.**  Barrel into the discomfort before she can armor up.

**KENDALL**
Okay.  Okay.  I’ll ask her things.  A million miles an hour.  Catch her before she can deflect.

But now she’s scratching her head.

**KENDALL**
Shit. *What* do I ask?

She flips open her notebook.  A blank page.  Scribbles the top line:

**QUESTIONS FOR KATHY**

She starts listing:

- What song do you still hate playing live?
- What did your mom get wrong about you?
- What’s the most embarrassing thing you ever wore on stage—on *purpose*?
- Who do you write for when you’re not trying to impress anybody?
- If the band ended tomorrow, what would you still be proud of?
- Who do you not trust in the industry? (Besides obvious names.)
- Do you actually like Gilley, or do you just perform around him?
- What’s the one thing no one has ever dared ask you?

She stops.  Reads that last one again.  Smiles.

**KENDALL**
Okay, Espich.  Let’s *dance.*

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – BACKSTAGE DRESSING ROOM CORRIDOR – MARCH 21, 1998 – 3:57 PM**

The band hits the stage in four hours.  Crew is bustling.  Someone is swearing about gaffer tape. **Kendall Weatherby**, combat boots, notebook, and a battered **microcassette recorder**, walks like she’s storming the Bastille.  She checks the hallway, sees the cracked-open dressing room door: **KATHY ESPICH** inside, **barefoot**, sitting on the counter, lighting a cigarette under a vent, already in full pre-show warpaint.

**KENDALL** (knocks once, enters before permission)
Got five minutes?

**KATHY** (snorts)
You got three and a half, and I eat timewasters for lunch.

**KENDALL**
Good.  I’m recording.

She presses the red **“REC”** button and *lets it fly*:

**KENDALL**
How does queer inform your writing now that you’re sleeping with women?  What lesson did you actually learn from posing nude in *Playboy*?  What the hell are you doing snorting coke again?  Are you still pissed about how you tanked on *120 Minutes*?  How do you square your lover collection with Cremeans’s moral superiority complex?  What did you *really* think when Jeff got married last year?  What kind of car do you drive—seriously?  Do you regret quitting guitar, or are you relieved it’s not part of your persona anymore?  Why the hell did you vote for Bill Clinton?  And would you vote for a Republican this fall if he’s on the ballot?

**Silence.**

The cigarette crackles in Kathy’s fingers.  She leans back against the mirror.  Eyeliner sharp enough to wound.

Then?

**KATHY**
Jesus Christ, Weatherby.  You been saving that up, or is this just foreplay?

**KENDALL**
I figure I’ve got maybe five minutes before you tell me to fuck off, so I’m burning all the tape.

**KATHY** (smiling)
You don’t even breathe between ‘em.  Like a goddamn jackhammer with a journalism degree.

**KENDALL**
Was that a compliment?

**KATHY**
You’ll know it if I slap you.

She flicks ash into a bottle cap.  Eyes narrow.  Something… sparks.

**KATHY**
Alright.  You want answers?

She hops off the counter.

**KATHY**
Then close the door.  You just stepped on the landmine.  Might as well ride the explosion.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – DRESSING ROOM – CONTINUED**

The door clicks shut behind Kendall.  The **tape is rolling**.  Kathy leans on the edge of the counter, cigarette still burning, eyes locked on Kendall with a *look that strips varnish*.

**KATHY**
You wanna know how queerness works?

**(beat)**
Okay.

She exhales smoke like punctuation.

**KATHY**
Just because I’m sleeping with women right now doesn’t mean I’ve stopped sleeping with men.  It’s not a fucking *trade-in policy*.

**(beat)**
Queerness doesn’t mean I graduated from dick.  It means the *entire structure*—who we’re told to want, how we’re told to want them, when and where and under what moral umbrella—that entire system?  It’s bullshit.

**(smiling)**
So if you need to put a label on it to feel safe in your article, try this: *I fuck who I want.  Full stop.*

**KENDALL** (nods slowly)
Deal with it?

**KATHY**
Grow up.

She taps ash, never breaking eye contact.

**KATHY**
You think the fans care?  Some do.  Some want me to be the angry lesbian messiah.  Some want me to kiss a girl in a music video and then pretend it was just *art*.  None of them actually want the truth.

**(beat)**
But I tell it anyway.  Because I’d rather confuse them than lie to them.

**KENDALL**
And what about the band?

**KATHY**
They already know.  They always knew.  Hell, Gilley’s probably drawing a chart somewhere.  Jim keeps it to himself.  Jeff’s the only one who ever asked why.

**(pause)**
