I told him: because I didn’t want my desire policed by anyone—not the Church, not the scene, and sure as hell not my own nostalgia.

**KENDALL**
That’s going in print.

**KATHY**
Good.  Make sure the font’s bold.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – DRESSING ROOM – CONTINUED**

Kendall barely finishes her sentence.

**KENDALL**
So… the *Playboy* shoot—what did that—

**KATHY** (interrupting)
Oh, you want to know about *that*?

**(leans forward)**
Yeah, it taught me something.  It taught me that I have the **best-looking body in the entire rock music business.**  *Bar none.*

She ashes the cigarette with a deliberate flick, then keeps going.

**KATHY**
And it taught me that even in **this United States, in the year 1998**,  even *Playboy*—fucking *Playboy*—is **afraid of a woman’s clit.**

**(snorts)**
Goddamn.

**(beat)**
Do you know how many times we paced that stage at **Bogart’s**, trying to line up that shot *exactly right*?  Three people.  Three different people with measuring tape and protractors and too much lighting anxiety.

**(grinning now)**
I used a goddamn **notecard**, Weatherby.

**KENDALL**
A notecard?

**KATHY**
Yup.  Held it right over my pussy.  That card was my test marker.  If the notecard showed up in the shot? *Too much.*  If it didn’t?  We had *just enough.*

**(beat)**
My ass was **marked** on that stage. **To the millimeter.**

She stubs out the cigarette.

**KATHY**
I showed what I showed because I **wanted** to.  Not because it was easy, not because it was “empowering,” not because it was some edgy brand play.  I did it because I was sick of men telling me where my mystery ends and their comfort begins.

**(locking eyes)**
Quote me.

**KENDALL**
I will.

**KATHY**
And don’t soften it.  Make the text scream.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – DRESSING ROOM – CONTINUED**

Kathy’s cigarette is out, but her fire?  Still burning.  She taps the table once.

**KATHY**
And as for the **cocaine**—I’m not admitting anything on the record.

**(beat)**
But *off the record*?

She leans closer.  Drops her voice just enough to make Kendall lean in.

**KATHY**
Just like *anybody else* in the Hollywood/media/entertainment complex—*yes*, sometimes, I **do inhale.**  Thank you very much.

She grins, sits back like that’s the most polite felony ever committed.  Kendall’s about to shift to the next topic, but Kathy cuts her off:

**KATHY**
*120 Minutes.*

**(beat)**
That was probably the **lowest moment** of my media career.  And I’m not being dramatic.  I’m being **perfectionally embarrassed**.

**(leaning forward again)**
Off the record?  *Yeah.*  It was bad.  Real bad.  I cratered so hard I *almost* asked Jeff to write me a statement.  That’s how far gone I was.

**(beat)**
But *on the record*?

She sits up straight.  Grabs the mic for a second, mock-formal:

**KATHY**
*I don’t give a fuck.*

**(lets go, laughing)**
Put that in bold, Kendall.

**KENDALL**
I might tattoo it.

**KATHY**
Good.  Just make sure you get the punctuation right.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – DRESSING ROOM – CONTINUED**

Kendall’s flipping pages, trying to keep up.  The tape is *definitely still rolling*.  Kathy’s leaning forward, the mirror behind her catching the sharp line of her jaw like a spotlight.

**KATHY**
And you want to know about my **car**?

She grins—*wolfishly*.

**KATHY**
I drive a **Ford Mustang SVT Cobra**.

**(beat)**
Supercharged. 305 horsepower.  Jet black, no apologies.  Goes from zero to *fuck you* in **under three seconds**.

She stubs her cigarette with a flourish.

**KATHY**
You hear me, Weatherby?

**KENDALL**
Clear as exhaust.

**KATHY**
Good.  Because everything I do—*everything*—comes with that engine under the hood.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – DRESSING ROOM – CONTINUED**

Kathy’s momentum slows.  The fire’s still there, but her voice softens—just slightly.

**KATHY**
And as for **Cremeans**?

She pauses.  The first real pause since the interview started.

**KATHY**
He’s… *saintly*.

**(beat)**
Doesn’t judge me.  That’s rare.  That’s—*shit*, that’s basically impossible in this business.

**(quiet)**
And it’s good he doesn’t.  Because if anyone ever *really* judged me?

**(another beat)**
They’d probably find me guilty.  Because I live in guilt.

**(shakes her head, laughing once—dry)**
And I will.

Then Kendall asks the last question—the quiet one, the personal one.

**KENDALL**
And Jeff?  When he got engaged last year?

Kathy blinks.  Looks off, like something just cracked in the floorboards.

**KATHY**
I, uh… huh.

She actually scratches the back of her neck.  First nervous tell of the conversation.

**KATHY**
This is awkward.

**(beat)**
I don’t have a comment about that.

**(more softly)**
Won't go to the wedding.  I wasn't invited.  Don’t know how he’s doing.

She looks down.  Lights a fresh cigarette she doesn’t really want.

**KATHY**
Next question?

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – DRESSING ROOM – CONTINUED**

The room is thick with the last of Kathy’s cigarette smoke and the kind of **truth that doesn’t need to be shouted** to hit like a punch.  She exhales through her nose, cool and steady.

**KATHY**
As for *regrets* about playing guitar?

**(beat)**
Not a goddamn one.

She leans forward, fingers miming across an invisible keyboard on the table.

**KATHY**
Now I’ve got **piano**.  And I can create something *rich*.  I can make it sound like a man.  I can make a woman *come* with just three notes.

**(softly, eyes far away)**
I can *soar*.  From the 18th century to the 21st.  All on **88 keys**.

Kendall doesn’t say a word.  Just lets her ride the wave.  And then Kathy’s eyes shift.

**KATHY**
And *you*, of all people—*you* wonder why I voted for **Bill Clinton**?

**(leans in)**
Because I believed.

**(beat)**
I really believed the Cold War was *over.*  I believed in a town called *Hope*.  I believed things were going to be **different**.

**(voice cracks, just slightly)**
I really thought… we were *done* with the lies.  That this was a *new era.*

She laughs—bitter, not broken.

**KATHY**
And now we’ve got **Republican Light** in the White House.  And say what you want about the *previous* Bush, at least that one kept his *zipper up.*

**(beat)**
Now we got this *shit-for-brains*…

She doesn’t finish the sentence.  Just stares past Kendall at the wall.

**KATHY**
It doesn’t make me mad.

**(quiet now)**
It makes me *sad.*

Silence.  Then, the tape clicks.  Kendall looks down—tape’s run out.  Kathy just smiles faintly.

**KATHY**
Perfect timing.

---


## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – DRESSING ROOM HALLWAY – MOMENTS LATER**

The door swings shut behind Kathy with a soft *click*.  Kendall just stands there for a second.  Still holding the recorder.  Blinking.  Like someone who *accidentally summoned a goddess and survived*.

**KENDALL** (quietly, to herself)
Did that just happen?

She stares down at the **tiny plastic tape recorder**, still warm in her hand.

**KENDALL**
*Did that just actually fucking happen?*

She checks the time counter: **6:37.**  Six minutes and thirty-seven seconds.  That’s all it took for Kathy to **burn down eight years of media malfeasance and rebuild it in her own image**.

**KENDALL**
Goddamn.  I really gotta get a better tape recorder.

She turns it over like it’s *done its time*.

**KENDALL**
This thing’s gonna be the death of me.

She shoves it in her pocket.  Starts walking down the hallway, adrenaline still buzzing in her fingertips.

**KENDALL** (sotto)
Holy shit.  I just got the story.

---

## **INT.  CORE STATES CENTER – PRODUCTION OFFICE – LATER THAT EVENING**

**Jeff Cremeans** sits behind a folding table, surrounded by venue maps, setlist revisions, and three distinct kinds of black pens.  **Kendall** steps in and wordlessly **places the tape recorder on the table.**

**KENDALL**
Start it.  First sixty seconds.

Cremeans eyes her.  Presses **play**.  The tape hisses.  Then **Kathy’s voice hits like a thunderclap**, cutting through with a raw, defiant cadence.  Cremeans listens.  Sixty seconds in, he stops the tape.  Leans back.  Smirks.

**CREMEANS**
I’ve lived it.

**(beat)**
You think this is odd?

He gestures around them.

**CREMEANS**
I think this is **Friday night.**

Kendall exhales, still bracing for the fallout.

**CREMEANS**
And you’re worried about Kathy vetoing you?

**(waves it off)**
She didn’t take a verbal swing at you.  She didn’t dress you down, didn’t throw anything.  Hell—she *invited you back*, didn’t she?

**KENDALL**
She said, “Close the door.”  Then she detonated.

**CREMEANS**
Then that’s your first gateway.

**(beat)**
You *clearly* passed through.

He taps the tape recorder once.

**CREMEANS**
So welcome to Level Two.

---

## **EXT.  TIDAL BASIN – WASHINGTON, D.C. – APRIL 1, 1998 – MORNING**

It’s **April Fool’s Day**, but the city doesn’t look like a joke.  It looks like **a painting.**  Cherry blossoms explode across every branch, soft pink petals drifting through the air like confetti for a party no one scheduled.  Tourists swarm.  Joggers dodge strollers.  The Washington Monument stands guard through the haze.  **Kendall** sits on a bench with a coffee in hand.  Her tape recorder is off.  Her notebook is open.  But for once, **she’s not writing anything down.**  She’s **running inventory.**  In her head.

**KENDALL’S MENTAL CHECKLIST – APRIL 1, 1998**

**D.C.**
Home, but not anymore.  Just a pit stop with memories and overpriced lattes.

**Gore's office:** Burned the bridge, salted the earth, and left no forwarding address.  No regrets.

**Jim:** Still a question mark.  Still kind.  Still makes her nervous.  Still the only one she dreams about when she sleeps too hard on tour buses.

**Cremeans:** Gave her the nod.  She’s in—maybe not for life, but definitely for the season.  Trusts her.  That counts.

**Kathy:** Didn’t kill her.  Invited her back. *That’s a miracle.*  And that interview?  Still echoes in her head every morning she opens the notebook.

**Gilley:** Hasn’t made a second move. *Yet.*  Reminder: Keep smiling neutral and knees pointed away.

**Jeff:** Still orbiting.  Still unreadable.  Still the smartest man in the room who hasn’t finished his sentence.

**Mission:** Tell the truth.  Remember everything.  Build the archive.  Don’t flinch.

She sips her coffee.  Watches a kid chase petals across the grass.

**KENDALL**  (to herself)
Alright, Weatherby.  April’s here.  Let’s see what happens next.

---

## **EXT.  DUPONT CIRCLE – CAFE PATIO – WASHINGTON, D.C. – APRIL 1, 1998 – AFTERNOON**

The cherry blossoms glow even this far from the Tidal Basin.  Kendall stirs her espresso with a plastic stick that’s melting slightly in the sun.  **Marci**, crisp blazer, Hill badge tucked out of sight, drops into the seat across from her, pulling off her sunglasses.

**MARCI**
God, it’s good to see you.  You look… not dead.

**KENDALL**
*Yet.*

**MARCI**
Listen—might be smart to update your resume.  People are circling wagons. 2000 is coming fast.  This summer’s gonna be the **money primary**, and after that, we start sorting who lives and dies in Iowa.  You should get back in the mix.

**KENDALL**
When was the last time *you* changed the world?

Marci pauses.  Smiles thin.

**KENDALL**
Because from where I sit—your team’s been in power for six years.  And here’s what we’ve got:

**(starts counting off on her fingers)**

- A prison-industrial complex on steroids.
- A “crime bill” that turned three generations of Black men into ghosts.
- Hundreds of thousands dead in Africa because nobody in the Situation Room gave a shit about *non-strategic bodies*.
- Yugoslavia? *Poof.* You can kiss *Kosovo* goodbye too.

**(beat)**
Nice work on that *Nobel Peace Prize*.  Looks like you can cross that off the dream board.

Marci tries to interject.  Kendall holds up a hand.

**KENDALL**
And you remember that thing we all used to say?

**(leans in, mocking gently)**
*“Butter, not guns”?*

**(sits back)**
Yeah, that aged well.  We were gonna cut defense spending, remember?  Reinvest in *people*.  Social programs.  Public schools.  Mental health.  That was the promise.

**(coldly)**
Now all we’ve got is buttered toast and more goddamn missiles.

**(quiet)**
Butter, not guns my flat ass.

Marci exhales.  Stares.

**MARCI**
So you’re not coming back?

**KENDALL**
Depends.

**(smiling faintly)**
You guys got a band?

---

## **EXT.  DUPONT CIRCLE – CAFE PATIO – CONTINUED**

Marci sips her sparkling water, adjusting her posture like she’s about to deliver a TED Talk.

**MARCI**
I mean—come on, Kendall.  A **rock band**?  That’s where you’ve landed?

**(scoffs)**
Aren’t they the ones with the *chick who showed her boobs* in *Playboy*?

Kendall doesn’t even blink.  Just **slowly turns her head** and gives Marci the kind of stare that can **age a person ten years**.

**KENDALL**
Jesus, Marci.

**(deadpan)**
Have you paid attention to *any* college class since the goddamn **Port Huron Statement**?

Marci blinks, confused.

**KENDALL**
Ever read it?  “Authenticity.  Participation.  Real democracy.  Rejection of hollow institutions.”  That ring a bell?  No?

**(leans in, fire rising)**
This band—yeah, the one with the woman you can’t stop sexualizing—they talk about rage.  They write about bodies, power, *capital*, grief, addiction.  They hit notes that blow out eardrums and *wake people the fuck up.*

**(beat)**
And Kathy Espich’s tits?  Are still less exposed than most of the **cowardice in your donor memos.**

Marci goes quiet.

**KENDALL**
So yeah.  I joined a band.  Because they *still believe they can say something that matters.*

**(pause)**
You should try it sometime.

She stands.  Marci stares.

**MARCI**
…You gonna vote in 2000?

**KENDALL**
*Still deciding who deserves it.*

---

## **EXT.  TIDAL BASIN – THOMAS JEFFERSON MEMORIAL – LATE AFTERNOON**

The sun’s slanting low across the **cherry blossom petals**, turning the basin’s surface into a mirror of gold and pink.  **Kendall** stands at the steps of the **Jefferson Memorial**, coffee in one hand, her notebook clutched under her arm.  She looks up at the statue.

**KENDALL** (to herself)
Well.  There you are, Tommy.

Jefferson stands tall in bronze, eyes pointed across the water, coat tails immortalized in a breeze that no longer blows.

**KENDALL**
Flawed as hell.  Contradictory.  Kind of a hypocrite.  *Sharp dresser, though.*

She walks slowly inside, standing beneath the rotunda, reading the inscriptions on the walls.  She knows them all.  Hell, she’s quoted them in memos, on panels, at fundraisers.  Now they sound… quieter.  Sadder.  Truer.

**KENDALL**
You owned slaves and wrote about liberty.  You invented ideals and broke most of them.  You scribbled *life, liberty, and the pursuit of happiness*, and left “equality” up for debate.

**(beat)**
But you still **wrote it down**.

She looks out across the water.

**KENDALL**
They gave you the best spot in town.  Right here.  On the basin.  Where everything blossoms—and everything’s rotting underneath.

**(softly)**
You were a walking contradiction.

She sighs.

**KENDALL**
Guess I’m in good company.

She turns and walks down the steps—back to the street, to the noise, to the tour.  But her spine’s a little straighter.

---

## **INT.  FAMILY KITCHEN – CLARKSVILLE, TENNESSEE – EVENING – APRIL 2, 1998**

Faint hum of an old ceiling fan.  The smell of something grilled lingering in the air.  A window open just enough to let in the sound of frogs starting up outside.  **Kendall** sits at the table, hands wrapped around a glass of sweet tea like it’s an anchor.  Across from her, her **father**—retired Army, practical to the bone—sits in his worn flannel and listens.  She looks up, clears her throat once.

**KENDALL**
I made a choice.

He doesn’t flinch.  Just waits.

**KENDALL**
Not fully official yet.  I’m still waiting on the actual offer.  But I know what I’m gonna do.

**(beat)**
It’s been… hell.  The last three weeks.  New cities every 48 hours, screaming matches in dressing rooms, policy ghosts in my dreams.  I interviewed a woman who could end nations with her voice.  I watched a band function like a military operation with a drug problem.  And I think—*somehow*—that I’m supposed to be there.

He takes a sip of his coffee.  Then:

**DAD**
You *sure*?

**KENDALL**
Not sure of the future.  But sure of the decision.

**(beat)**
It’s messy.  It’s unpredictable.  It’s not on a GS schedule.

**(softly)**
But it’s *real*.  And I don’t think I’ve felt *real* since before the midterms.

He nods once.  Looks at her like he’s trying to measure the weight behind her eyes.

**DAD**
Well.  I don’t know what kind of retirement plan a rock band’s got.

**KENDALL**
Neither do I.

**DAD**
But you’ll figure it out.

**(beat)**
And if you don’t—hell, you’ll build one.

She exhales.  Just sits in that for a moment.

**KENDALL**
Yeah.  I think I might.

---

## **INT.  FAMILY KITCHEN – CLARKSVILLE, TENNESSEE – NIGHT**

The light’s low now.  Bugs chirp just outside the screen door.  Kendall’s finished her tea.  Her **father** stands, walks to a drawer near the fridge, and rustles through it like he’s looking for a screwdriver.  Instead, he pulls out something small, heavy, metallic.  A **coin**.  He walks back, holds it between two fingers, and drops it in front of her on the table with a *clink*.

**DAD**
There.

**KENDALL**
What’s this?

**DAD**
That’s the first commemorative coin I ever got.  **Berlin Brigade. 1975.**

She picks it up.  Turns it in her hand.  Worn.  Engraved.  Real weight.

**DAD**
It says “exceptional service.”  What it meant was—I was able to smuggle Coors Light from Colorado into Berlin in bulk.

**(leans in, mock serious)**
We’re not telling your mother that part.

Kendall laughs.  He smiles.

**DAD**
The point is—You can do weird things.  Odd things.  *Different* things.

**(beat)**
And still make a difference.

He nods toward the coin.

**DAD**
Also—when you’re in Berlin?  That’ll still get you free drinks.  Probably more now than it did then.

She raises an eyebrow.

**KENDALL**
Wait—do you mean a **coin challenge**?

**DAD**
Goddamn right I do.  You walk into a bar, slap that down—if the other guy doesn’t have a coin, he buys the round.

**(smiling)**
That’s how you **score free booze**, Weatherby.

**KENDALL**
Jesus Christ, Dad!

**DAD**
Don’t knock it.  That coin saved me a fortune.

She closes her hand around it.  Smiles.

**KENDALL**
Thanks, Dad.

**DAD**
Don’t lose it.  And don’t forget what it means.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – PHILADELPHIA – APRIL 3, 1998 – EARLY MORNING**

Kendall’s suitcase is half-packed.  The coin her father gave her sits beside her notebook, catching the light.  Her **calendar** shows a penciled-in 2:30 p.m.  formal interview with **Jeff Cremeans**.  She stares at it.   Then scratches it out.

**KENDALL**
Nope.

She shuts the calendar, stands, and throws on her jacket.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I’ve been briefed, vetted, flung across four states and fourteen dressing rooms.  I’ve stood in the eye of Kathy’s storm, made Cremeans flinch, dodged Gilley, survived Jim, and earned Bill’s respect.

**(beat)**
I don’t need a *formal interview*.

**(pause)**
I need **Jeff Evans.**

She slams her notebook shut, throws her hair up, and marches away from the door.

### **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – PHILADELPHIA – MOMENTS LATER**

As she paces around the desk, she picks up the desk phone and mutters:

**KENDALL**
Where the fuck is Jeff?

She dials Cremeans.

### **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – SAME TIME – APRIL 3, 1998**

Kendall leans against the bedroom wall, phone pressed to her ear.

**CREMEANS (PHONE)**
I try not to swear very much.  But *how long did it take you to figure it out?*

**KENDALL**
Figure *what* out?

**CREMEANS**
The *gatekeepers*.

**(beat)**
Why they exist.  Who they are.  Why you’ve got to go *through* them, but never *around* them.

Kendall exhales.  The hallway goes quiet around her.

**KENDALL**
You tell me.

**CREMEANS**
Because some people are talent.  Some people are sound.  Some people are soul.  And some people—*the gatekeepers*—they’re the only ones who know where the **truth** gets locked up.

**(quiet)**
Jeff Evans is one of them.  And he doesn’t give you trust.  You take it.  You *earn it*—slow, patient, strange.

**KENDALL**
So I was never supposed to schedule the formal interview.

**CREMEANS**
Nope.

**KENDALL**
And what would’ve happened if I had?

**CREMEANS**
He’d have blown you off.

**KENDALL**
Thanks for the heads-up.

**CREMEANS**
*You called me.  Not the other way around.*

**(beat)**
Now go find him.

---

## **EXT.  PHILADELPHIA – MARKET STREET – APRIL 3, 1998 – LATE MORNING**

Kendall walks fast down the sidewalk, notebook in her shoulder bag, coin in her jacket pocket, **mind racing faster than her boots can carry her.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Okay.  Logic problem.

**(beat)**
Where do you find Jeff Evans on a Friday morning in Philly?

Option A: **Near Independence Hall**, muttering about democratic erosion and federalist irony, probably scribbling a lyric on the back of a SEPTA transfer.

Option B: **On top of a blonde.** Possibly his wife.  Hopefully his wife.

Because if it’s his wife, there’s a *slim* chance he’ll come up for air.  If it’s not?  Game over, and I’m not getting a callback until Sunday.

**(beat)**
So… fifty-fifty.

**She slows as she nears the Liberty Bell Pavilion.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Odds are better that if he’s in his head, he’s **somewhere near here**—chasing ghosts of the revolution, trying to feel righteous about the wreckage.

She stops.  Looks around.  Tourists, families, field trips.  She spots a tall, dark-haired man sitting on a bench near the Bell center’s glass wall, **legs crossed, wearing headphones**, a **legal pad** in his lap, pen flicking rapidly across the page.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Fifty-fifty, baby.  And I just **hit the odds.**

She approaches—quiet, steady.  Doesn’t speak yet.  Just watches him scribble, cross out, write again.  Because you don’t interrupt a gatekeeper.  You **wait for the door to open.**

---

## **EXT.  LIBERTY BELL PAVILION – PARK BENCH – CONTINUED**

**Jeff Evans** doesn’t look up right away.  His pen keeps moving.  Then stops.  Then, without turning:

**JEFF**
You want to understand me?

Kendall stands silently.

**JEFF**
Then figure out what the **Northwest Ordinance** is.

Now he looks up.  Headphones hang around his neck.  His eyes are sharp, but not unfriendly.

**JEFF**
Congress only did two things right under the Articles of Confederation.  One—they called it quits and let the Constitution get written.

**(beat)**
The other was the Northwest Ordinance.  *1787.* That law built **Ohio**.  And the **Midwest**.

**(counting off on his fingers)**
Michigan—and by God, I hate that state up north with every fiber of my soul.  Indiana.  Illinois.  Wisconsin.  Even the Iron Range. *Minnesota, you know.*

**(leans forward slightly)**
You want to understand me?  Understand *that*.

**KENDALL**
The legislation?

**JEFF**
The **principle**.

**(beat)**
A system that tried to bring **order** to chaos.  Territory to nationhood.  Ideas into *grids and deeds and borders*.

**(softer)**
And it gave us a place to become something else.

He leans back.

**JEFF**
You understand that piece of legislation?  You’ll understand me.  You’ll understand the **band**.

**(smiling, slightly dangerous)**
You’ll understand *everything*.

Kendall’s eyes narrow, taking it in.

**JEFF**
Because one thing is always true.

**(beat)**
It’s **Ohio versus the world**.

**(quiet)**
Don’t ever forget it.

---

## **EXT.  LIBERTY BELL PAVILION – PARK BENCH – CONTINUED**

The breeze picks up, soft and cool.  Tourists shuffle by, none of them noticed that **Kendall Weatherby** just found the **axis of the band’s universe.**  She tilts her head, studying Jeff.

**KENDALL**
Do you do this on purpose?

Jeff doesn’t flinch.  Doesn’t blink.  Just smiles that sideways smile that makes you wonder what you’ve stepped into.

**JEFF**
Would *you* do it any other way?

He shrugs, easy.

**JEFF**
If you’ve got advice, I’ll listen to it.

**(beat)**
But I’ll ignore you in the long run.

**KENDALL**
Of course you will.

**JEFF**
I don’t know any other way to do it but **my** way.

**(quiet)**
It hurts.  But I’m usually fine.

Kendall nods.  Doesn’t press further.  She’s not here to change him.  She’s just here to *record what happens when he moves through the world.*  She finally sits down beside him.

**KENDALL**
Then let me tell it right.

Jeff taps the edge of his legal pad.

**JEFF**
You’ll know when you’re close.  The page’ll start bleeding back at you.

---

## **EXT.  LIBERTY BELL PAVILION – WALKING AWAY – LATE MORNING**

Kendall’s steps are quick now, light.  Her brain’s on fire. **Notebook out, pen uncapped, writing while walking.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
He hurts, but he’s usually fine.

**(beat)**
That’s it.  That’s the line.  That’s the piece.

No need for a lede.  No fancy structure.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
It’s not a quote.  It’s a **diagnosis**.  It’s the **blueprint of Jeff Evans**.  And maybe the whole goddamn band.

She’s weaving through crowds like a woman on a mission, scribbling as fast as the ink will go.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
He hurts, but he’s usually fine.  That’s how he writes.  That’s how he talks.  That’s how he lives, and it’s how we listen.

**(beat)**
You want to understand Commuted?  Start there.

She stops at a bench, tears out a clean page, and writes at the top:

**He Hurts, But He’s Usually Fine**

Underneath it, she scrawls:

- Northwest Ordinance
- Ohio vs.  the World
- Confessions without apology
- Damage as methodology
- No advice taken, but all of it heard
- This is how we get the songs
- This is how we survive him

She exhales.

**KENDALL**
This is gonna be *banging*.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – PHILADELPHIA – NIGHT**

Laptop open. **Blank document.  Cursor blinking.**  Kendall sits cross-legged on the bed, hair tied up, T-shirt loose, mug of something black and medicinal next to her.  She cracks her knuckles, cracks her neck.  She’s ready.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
This isn’t liner notes.  This isn’t a press kit or a blog blurb or a backstage puff piece.

**(beat)**
This is a ***record.***

She types:

**“He Hurts, But He’s Usually Fine”**
*A Field Report from the Edge of Commuted*

And then it pours.

**EXCERPT: FIRST PARAGRAPH**

If you want to understand Commuted, don’t start with the setlists.  Don’t start with the record sales, or the scandals, or the fact that half the band can’t make it through a four-state tour without starting a fire, figurative or otherwise.  Start with this: Jeff Evans hurts, but he’s usually fine.  That’s not a diagnosis.  That’s a *design flaw* turned into an operating system.  And the band runs on it.

---

**He Hurts, But He’s Usually Fine — A Field Report from the Edge of Commuted**
*By Kendall Weatherby – April 4, 1998*

If you want to understand Commuted, don’t start with the setlists.  Don’t start with the record sales, or the scandals, or the fact that half the band can’t make it through a four-state tour without starting a fire, figurative or otherwise.  Start with this:  **Jeff Evans hurts, but he’s usually fine.**

That’s not a diagnosis.  That’s a design flaw turned into an operating system.  And the band runs on it.

**I.  The Quiet Core: Jeff Evans**

I found Jeff Evans sitting across from the Liberty Bell, scribbling on a legal pad like he was drafting a treaty.  When I asked him if he does this—this labyrinthine, contradictory way of existing—on purpose, he said, *"Would you do it any other way?"* and smiled.  He told me to understand him by understanding the Northwest Ordinance of 1787.  Not in passing—like a reference—but as a thesis. *"That law built Ohio,"* he said. *"Understand that, and you understand me.  You understand the band.  You understand everything."*

Jeff speaks in legislation.  He breathes in code.  And yet, every once in a while, he bleeds a line like:  **"It hurts.  But I’m usually fine."**  You can build a universe off that sentence.  Commuted did.

**II.  The Firestarter: Kathy Espich**

My interview with Kathy lasted 6 minutes and 37 seconds.  She lit a cigarette, tore open a vein, and didn’t flinch once.  We talked queerness, *Playboy*, cocaine, failure, Clinton, and the collapse of hope.  She told me she can make a woman come in three piano notes and that she drove a Mustang SVT Cobra because it goes from zero to “fuck you” in under three seconds.  She told the truth like it was an act of war.  And she made me realize this band doesn’t do media.  They do **mythology**.

*"I showed what I showed because I wanted to show it,"* she said of the *Playboy* shoot. *"Quote me."*

So I am.

**III.  The Archive and the Fire**

I used to work in policy.  I drafted memos for people who promised hope and delivered silence.  I sat in rooms where no one remembered the truth.  Now I work in the splash zone of a band that believes if you say the right three words in the right order, you can save someone’s life—or ruin your own.  They are chaos and calculus.  They are sex and sound.  They are **Ohio versus the world**.  And I am their recorder.  Not just their public voice, but their private archive.  The memory.  The counter-narrative.

So here’s what I’ve learned:
They all hurt.
They’re all usually fine.
And they tell the truth—when they think no one’s listening.

**I’m always listening.**

—KW

---

## **INT.  BACKSTAGE GREENROOM – BALTIMORE ARENA – APRIL 4, 1998 – LATE NIGHT**

Kendall hands the printed draft to **Jeff Cremeans**, who skims it in silence.  Reads the last line.  Flips back.  Scans again.  Then he looks up.

**CREMEANS**
Is it your intention to do a **10% effort** on *everything* for the next, say, **three days** that you’re still employed?

Kendall blinks.

**CREMEANS**
Because if that’s your model, I’d like to adjust my expectations *right now.*

**(beat)**
I told you I wanted **4,000 words**.  You gave me **461**.

He places the pages on the table between them.  Neatly.  Precisely.

**CREMEANS**
So are you going to do what you’re told to do—or should I hand this assignment off to someone who **doesn’t think every paragraph is a revolution**?

**(quietly)**
Because I sign your paycheck, Weatherby.

Long silence.  Kendall stares at the pages.  Then at him.

**KENDALL**
You’re right.

**(beat)**
This is a **first strike.**

She picks up the pages.  Tucks them back into her bag.

**KENDALL**
Next one will draw blood.

### **INT.  TOUR BUS – MIDNIGHT**

Kendall sits at her laptop, the glow illuminating her determined face.  The cursor blinks at the end of her article.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
*“He Hurts, But He’s Usually Fine”*—4,000 words, exactly.  Not a word more, not a word less.

She hits 'Save' and leans back, exhaling deeply.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Cremeans will scrutinize every sentence for impact.  Gore would dissect every paragraph for structure and policy alignment.  Who’s more terrifying?

She chuckles to herself.

**KENDALL**
At least Cremeans doesn’t make me write memos about memos.

---

## **INT.  CREMEANS’ OFFICE – NEXT MORNING**

Cremeans reads the article, his expression unreadable.  He finishes, sets the pages down, and picks up the phone.

**KENDALL**
Here we go.

**KENDALL**
Hello?

She slaps the manuscript down and says:

**KENDALL**
***Are you happy now, Cremeans?***

And it lands like thunder—**4,928 words** of searing truth, reconstructed history, unflinching character dissection, and fire-laced confessionals.  Kendall Weatherby doesn’t write press. **She writes scripture**.  And this time, she doesn’t hold back—not on anyone.

Cremeans reads it.  Every word.

**CREMEANS**
This isn’t a no.  It’s a *see me Monday.*

She’s not fired.  She’s **in**.  Deep.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL LOBBY BAR – DALLAS, TEXAS – NIGHT – APRIL 5, 1998**

The band just wrapped a brutal back-to-back weekend.  Everyone’s scattered—some asleep, some *missing,* and some **hovering around the minibar**.  **Kendall** strides into the hotel bar like a woman on a mission.  Fresh from uploading a 5,000-word heartbomb, **buzzing with adrenaline, exhaustion, and desire.**

She checks the bar.  No Gilley.  No Kathy.  No Cremeans.  But then—

Back corner booth.  Dark shirt.  Baseball cap.  Headphones around his neck.  **Jim Brown.**  Alone.  Nursing a Guinness.  She approaches, casual but coiled tight.

**KENDALL**
You hiding, or waiting?

**JIM** (looks up, small smile)
Little of both.  You?

**KENDALL**
Looking for trouble.

**JIM** (sips his beer)
You find it yet?

**KENDALL**
Not yet.

**(beat)**
But I’m good at locating what I need.

He raises an eyebrow.

**JIM**
Need a seat?

**KENDALL**
I need a drink.  Then I’ll decide if I need a seat.  Or if I’m just going to drag you upstairs.

**JIM** (chuckles, but eyes sharpen)
That direct, huh?

**KENDALL**
I just turned in a five-thousand-word expose on your band.  I think I’ve earned a few liberties.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL BAR – BACK CORNER – NIGHT CONTINUED**

Kendall stands there, casual but intense, her voice still echoing between them.

*“Or if I’m just going to drag you upstairs.”*

Jim lifts his beer.  Takes a sip.  Watches her over the rim.

**JIM**
You serious?

**KENDALL**
Why wouldn’t I be?

**JIM**
Because for the last three weeks, you’ve been *clocking hours like a campaign staffer*.  And so have I.

**(beat)**
And this?  This sounds like I’m being tested.

She smiles slightly, not denying it.

**KENDALL**
What if it is?

Jim leans forward, eyes narrowing—not hostile, just trying to read the energy.

**JIM**
Then I’d ask what happens if I pass.  Or what happens if I fail.

**(beat)**
Because I’ve kept it clean with you on purpose, Kendall.  You’re sharp, you’re fast, you’re in deep now.  I haven’t thought with my dick once.  And you haven’t acted like you wanted anyone to.

**KENDALL**
Until now.

**JIM**
Yeah.

**(sips again)**
So the question is—what changed?

She considers that.

**KENDALL**
Nothing.  And everything.

**(beat)**
I finished the piece.  I finally *said it all* out loud.  Now I’m just… here.  Still wired.  Still spinning.  And I want something real.  Not transactional.  Not scheduled.  Just **now**.

He’s silent for a long moment.  Then sets his beer down.

**JIM**
Okay.

**(quiet)**
But I’m not a vending machine.  You don’t push a button and get laid.

**KENDALL**
Wasn’t asking for one.  I’m asking for *you*.

He watches her.

**JIM**
Let’s finish the drink.  And then we’ll see if we’re still on the same page.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL BAR – BACK CORNER – NIGHT CONTINUED**

They sit in silence for a moment.  Jim drinks.  Kendall stares at her glass like it’s about to confess something for her.  She sets it down.  Slowly.  Looks him in the eye.

**KENDALL**
Okay.  You’re right.

**(beat)**
I came at this all sulfur and brimstone, and you called it.

He watches her.  Patient.

**KENDALL**
So let me tell you something real.  Not to prove anything.  Just so you know *who you’re sitting with.*

**(beat)**
I haven’t been in a relationship that lasted longer than six months since college.  Every time someone gets close, I find a reason to move cities or jobs or goals.  Sometimes I don’t even know I’m doing it until I’m already gone.

She pauses.

**KENDALL**
I used to tell myself it was because I was ambitious.  But really, it’s because I don’t know how to be *known* without being… *useful.*

She looks at him, eyes open, no shield.

**KENDALL**
You’re not a vending machine.  You’re a drummer who looks at people like you *hear them before they speak*.  And for what it’s worth?  This isn’t about getting laid.  This is about wanting to be held *like I’m a woman*, not a draft, or a deadline, or a utility.

**(beat)**
So that’s my truth.  Before anything else happens.

Jim takes a breath.  Quiet.

**JIM**
Awesome.

**(beat)**
You want another drink?

**KENDALL**
Only if you pour it yourself.

**JIM**
Deal.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL BAR – BACK CORNER – NIGHT CONTINUED**

**Jim Brown** watches her sip from her glass.  Not seductively.  Just… worn.  Present.  His hands rest around his pint, fingers tapping the condensation.

**JIM (V.O.)**
Three weeks ago, she fucked me like she was trying to banish every ghost she ever had.  Then she got dressed, called a cab, and *vanished.*  And I respected the hell out of that.  Now she’s back.

He looks at her, really looks.  Not the hair.  Not the lips.  The **posture**.  The slight shake in her hand from too much work and too little sleep.  The **ache in her eyes** that has nothing to do with sex.

**JIM (V.O.)**
So what is this?  Is she meat?  Throwing herself at me because I’ve got a platinum plaque and she’s riding adrenaline?  Or is she **that woman**—the one who made me feel like we shared *some kind of spark with mass*?  Because I don’t want a lay.  I want *her.*  If it’s her.

She catches him watching.  Not with hunger.  With curiosity.  With **care**.

**KENDALL**
You trying to figure out if I’m sincere?

**JIM**
I’m trying to figure out if you’re the same woman who walked out of my hotel room three weeks ago with fire in her veins and *my phone number* in her back pocket.

She nods once.  Steady.

**KENDALL**
I’m her.  Just tired.  And open.

Jim nods.  Slow.

**JIM**
Alright.

**(beat)**
Then let’s not fuck tonight.

**KENDALL** (beyond stunned)
…What?

**JIM**
Let’s *talk.*  Let’s sit on a bed with no clothes off and see if the fire’s still real.

**(smiles)**
If it is, we’ll know.  If it isn’t—well, I still owe you a drink.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL BAR – BACK CORNER – NIGHT CONTINUED**

Kendall exhales, half a smile curling up.

**KENDALL**
You men are something else.

**(beat)**
Alright.  Let’s do this.  Not sex. **This.** The choice.  The connection.  The possibility.

Jim sets down his glass, nods once, and raises a hand for the bartender.

**JIM**
Check, please.

The bartender nods.  No fuss.  Kendall grabs her coat.

**KENDALL**
No one ever says that when I’m not naked.  I like this version of the night.

**JIM**
You’ll like the next part too.

They walk out side by side.  Not touching.  But *closer*.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – JIM’S SUITE – LATER THAT NIGHT**

They sit on the edge of the bed.  Shoes off, jackets slung on chairs.  The room is still, the air between them charged but calm.  Jim leans forward, elbows on his knees.  He looks at Kendall, not hard, not soft—just **honest.**

**JIM**
Can I ask you something?

**KENDALL**
Yeah.

**JIM**
Why’d you walk out?

**(beat)**
Back then.  After Cincinnati.  You didn’t say a word.  Just… left.

Kendall doesn’t respond right away.  She watches her hands, fingers twisting slightly, then finally looks up.

**KENDALL**
Because it felt too real.  That weekend—we weren’t just hooking up.  You made space for me.  You *saw* me.  And I hadn’t felt that in years.

**(beat)**
I didn’t know how to handle it.  So I bailed before it could turn into something I couldn’t control.

Jim watches her.  Still.  Listening.

**KENDALL**
It’s a bad habit.  I don’t run for safety—I run from *connection*.

She sits back.  Not defensive.  Just *bare.*

**KENDALL**
That wasn’t about you.  It was about me not knowing what to do with something that didn’t feel like a mistake.

Silence stretches, but not uncomfortably.

Jim nods once.

**JIM**
That tracks.

He doesn’t press.

**JIM**
You’re here now.

**(beat)**
That matters more than the exit.

Kendall exhales.  Not relieved. **Understood.**

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – JIM’S SUITE – LATE NIGHT CONTINUED**

The silence after Jim’s words holds steady—safe, not stiff.  Kendall leans back against the headboard, arms loosely crossed, eyes fixed on a corner of the ceiling.

**KENDALL**
You want the real version?

**(beat)**
I walked out because I was at the edge of my rope.  Not metaphorically. *Literally*.  I was at wit’s end.

She pauses, breathes through it.

**KENDALL**
I had just walked out on the best-paying, worst job I’d ever had.  Quit the Hill.  Walked away from a sixteen-year roadmap because the people I worked for?  Sons of bitches.  Every last one of them.

**(beat)**
And the next day, I sat on my floor with an overdue rent notice and a stack of dead contacts and realized—I had no idea what the hell came next.

She looks at Jim, steady now.

**KENDALL**
So I took inventory.  And the only person I could think of who hadn’t treated me like a whore—in bed *or* in politics—was you.

**(beat)**
You didn’t ask for anything.  You didn’t take.  You didn’t twist it.

She rubs her hands together, like trying to warm herself.

**KENDALL**
My dad would be pissed if he knew I let people treat me like that.  Like my only currency was loyalty or silence or sex.  So I figured—*alright*.  Straighten up.  Fly right.

**(half-laughs)**
At least try.

Jim doesn’t say anything at first.  He just nods.  Then he leans back beside her, matching her position, not crowding it.

**JIM**
Trying counts.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – JIM’S SUITE – LATE NIGHT CONTINUED**

They lie side by side on the bed now, fully dressed, heads tilted toward the ceiling like they’re waiting for something to write across it.

**KENDALL**
So what about you?

**JIM**
What about me?

**KENDALL**
What’s your damage?

He grins faintly.  Not offended.  Just thoughtful.

**JIM**
None.

**(beat)**
I’m not damaged.

She turns her head slightly, skeptical.

**JIM**
I mean it.

**(beat)**
Single dad.  Small house.  Not a lot of money, but enough.  He packed my lunches.  Came to every practice.  Held shit down like it was a full-time job and a full-time mission.

**(beat)**
I had a good life.

He folds his hands over his chest.

**JIM**
Because he **bent over backwards** trying so goddamn hard to make sure it *felt* normal.  No drama.  No stories.  Just… decency.  Stability.  Quiet effort.

He glances at her.

**JIM**
That’s what raised me.  Not damage.  *Discipline.*

She lets that settle.  It’s not flashy.  It’s not tragic.  It’s *solid*.

**KENDALL**
I don’t even know how to process that.  That sounds… almost fictional.

**JIM**
I know.  And it’s the reason I never throw the first punch.  Because I already got the only thing I ever needed.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – JIM’S SUITE – LATE NIGHT CONTINUED**

Kendall turns her head, eyes soft but glinting.

**KENDALL**
That might be the sexiest thing I’ve ever heard.

Jim doesn’t miss a beat.

**JIM**
It’s the hair.  You’ll get used to it.

She laughs—low and surprised.

**KENDALL**
Oh, is that right?

**JIM**
Yep.

He rolls onto his side, looking at her fully now.  Calm.  Comfortable.

**JIM**
Nice thing about being bald is— once I shave it smooth?

**(beat)**
It won’t scruff the inside of your thighs.

Kendall blinks.  Smirks.  Laughs again, this time with her whole chest.

**KENDALL**
Jesus Christ.

**JIM**
You’re welcome.

**(beat)**
Told you I was raised right.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – JIM’S SUITE – NIGHT CONTINUED**

Kendall, laughing, still buzzing from his thigh comment, turns with a wicked grin and **grabs his shirt collar**.

**KENDALL**
You really shouldn’t have said that.

Jim lets her tug—just an inch—before lifting both hands like a ref calling a timeout.

**JIM**
Nope.  Nope.  Nope.  Nope.  Nope.

**(pause)**

**JIM**
Nope.

**(longer beat)**

**JIM**
You said hands-off.

Kendall doesn’t let go—but she eases up, amused and a little flushed.

**KENDALL**
I did, didn’t I?

**JIM**
You did.

**(beat)**
And I’m not gonna be the one who crosses that line just because the air got sweet.

She searches his face, sees it’s not rejection—it’s *sadness*.  She lets go of the collar, fingers brushing against his chest as she withdraws.

**KENDALL**
You’re infuriating.

**JIM**
I’ve been told.

He leans back against the pillows again, arms folded behind his head.

**JIM**
Now behave, Weatherby.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – JIM’S SUITE – NIGHT CONTINUED**

Kendall stands, stretching with casual theater, then eyes him across the room.

**KENDALL**
Would it be crossing a line if I changed into one of your big T-shirts and used it as a nightgown?
