She starts getting dressed.  Slowly.  Not because of modesty.  Because **fuck it**.

**KENDALL (muttering)**
You better drool, Jim Brown.  You better at least give me *that*.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – EARLY MORNING – POST-NUDITY**

Kendall finishes dressing as Jim snores in the corner.  She’s opted for a soft, oversized T-shirt—worn but clean.  Athletic bra underneath.  Loose.  Breathable. **Supportive, not suggestive.**
And gym shorts.  Not cute.  Not clingy. **Practical.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I just unlocked the code to touring while female.

**(beat)**
Loose clothing.  Athletic bra.  Big soft shirt.  Gym shorts that don’t ride up or ride out.

She ties her hair back.  Secure.  Efficient.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
It’s early May.  But this is Texas.  And it’s already **80 degrees at 6:30 in the goddamn morning.**

She slings her bag over her shoulder.  Looks down at her legs.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I’ve given enough to the patriarchy.  Y’all can live with the sight of my knees.

She grabs Jim’s untouched coffee and takes a long sip, watching him snore.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
This man is out like the dead.  And I’m the one who just invented tour chic.

She grins.

**KENDALL**
Let’s hit the fucking road.

---

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – EARLY MORNING – MOMENTS LATER**

Kendall slings her bag over her shoulder, coffee in hand, gym shorts swishing as she steps past the bed toward the door.  Behind her, **Jim shifts in the chair.** Still slouched.  Still snoring.  Then, without opening his eyes—

**JIM**
Nice shorts.

Kendall freezes mid-step.

**KENDALL**
You’ve gotta be kidding me.

No response.  Just a faint smile on Jim’s face.

His eyes stay closed.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
This man.  He doesn’t sleep.  He *charges.*

She takes another sip of his coffee.

**KENDALL**
Next time I’m stealing your socks too.

Still no response.  But the smile deepens.

---

## **INT.  TOUR BUS – FRONT CABIN – EARLY MORNING**

Kendall steps onto the bus, scanning the space with a soldier’s eye.  She finds her corner—**front right, near the window**, with just enough wall to lean against and just enough space to **pretend she’s invisible**.  She drops her bag, curls up, **coffee still in hand**, and exhales like she’s been sprinting for three weeks.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I just want to sleep.  That’s it.  That’s the dream.  That’s the arc.

Then—

**JEFF (O.S.)**
Yes.  We ought to be having a conversation.

**Kendall’s eyes snap open.**  Across from her, **Jeff Evans**, arms crossed, perfectly upright, **radiating “this is not optional”** energy.  From behind them, **Bill** quietly disappears toward the back of the bus—the members-only section.  The curtain swishes shut behind him like a trapdoor.  Kendall sighs.

**KENDALL**
I *really* want to sleep.

**(beat)**
But what do you got to say, Jeff?

**(tugs blanket around her)**
Can we make it quick?

Jeff sits across from her, stone-faced.

**JEFF**
I would like to discuss your favorite *Star Trek: The Next Generation* episode.

Kendall just stares.

**KENDALL**
What?

**JEFF**
I said—

**KENDALL**
No, I *heard* you.  I just…  didn’t know I was being interviewed by the Vulcan ambassador this morning.

**(beat)**
Fine.  You’re serious.  Okay.

---

## **INT.  TOUR BUS – FRONT CABIN – EARLY MORNING**

Kendall blinks, still wrapping her mind around being interrogated about **Star Trek** before sunrise.

**KENDALL**
Okay.  Favorite *Next Gen* episode?

She rubs her temples.

**KENDALL**
I mean, “The Inner Light” is haunting. “Chain of Command” is brutal.  But I always had a soft spot for “Darmok” because—

**JEFF**
Incorrect.

She blinks again.

**JEFF**
Any episode you name that is not *“The Measure of a Man”* is false.

Kendall just stares, open-mouthed.

**KENDALL**
You just baited me into an opinion only to **declare it invalid**?

**JEFF**
Correct.  *“The Measure of a Man”* is the definitive ethical argument of 24th-century science fiction.  It is the trial of humanity’s soul.  The question of autonomy, personhood, and the limits of institutional justice.

**(leans forward)**
It is also the episode that proves *Data* is more human than most officers on that ship.  Which, I would argue, is your situation right now.

Kendall groans, leans back against the window.

**KENDALL**
God, I need a nap before I start crying over android rights.

---

## **INT.  TOUR BUS – FRONT CABIN – EARLY MORNING**

Jeff watches Kendall with his usual unnerving precision.  No smile.  Just that **hyper-literal deadpan**.

**JEFF**
I am *absolutely* *fucking* with you right about now!

**(beat)**
But I gotta tell you—I saw you get on the bus and you look like *shit*.

**(tilts head)**
What the hell did you do last night?

**(mock concern)**
Were you fucking my man silly or something?

Kendall exhales and rubs her face like she’s trying to hold it together with sheer friction.

**KENDALL**
It was… something like that.

**(beat)**
No.  No, it wasn’t anything like that at all, Jeff.

**(sinks lower into her seat)**
It wasn’t anything at all like that.

Jeff leans back, folds his arms, lets the silence hang.

Then, with a totally unreadable shrug:

**JEFF**
Well.  There’s always *San Antonio*.

Kendall closes her eyes.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I am never going to sleep again.

---

## **INT.  TOUR BUS – FRONT CABIN – EARLY MORNING**

Kendall’s eyes are barely open now.  Head resting against the window.  The bus hums beneath them, wheels already rolling south.  Jeff watches her for a second longer.  Then:

**JEFF**
Hey.  Get some sleep, Ms.  Weatherby.

**(beat)**
When you’ve got some sleep, and you’ve got some time…

**(a little softer, still Jeff)**
Come tell me what kind of writers you like.

**(beat)**
But, uh…

He eyes her, eyebrows knit with flat honesty.

**JEFF**
Yeah, you look like shit.

**(nods once)**
Get some sleep.

Kendall lets out a breath, finally closing her eyes.

**KENDALL (murmuring)**
You’re such a charmer, Jeff.

**JEFF**
I know.

---

## **INT.  TOUR BUS – MOVING – LATER THAT MORNING**

The world around her is a **clattering mess**.  Crew boots on aluminum stairs.  Gilley arguing about soundcheck.  Someone rummaging through a fridge.  Tom the bus driver is **blasting AM radio**, some righteous talk about market volatility and farming subsidies.  A can rolls across the floor.  A laugh erupts.  Jeff mutters something scathing to someone off-mic.

**And yet—Kendall sleeps.**  Head against the window.  Hoodie pulled up.  Hands curled under her chin like a streetwise cat.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Turns out—If you’re tired *enough*?  You can sleep on a moving bus.  Even with twelve people crammed inside.  Even with metal clinks and foot stomps and caffeine-fueled **sharp commentary**.  Even with Driver Tom listening to **goddamn AM radio** like it’s sacred scripture.

She shifts slightly.  Doesn’t wake.  Just **breathes.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Oh dear Lord.  Oh dear Lord.  Oh dear *merciful* Lord…Thank you.

---

## **INT.  TOUR BUS – EARLY AFTERNOON – PARKED OUTSIDE ALAMODOME**

Kendall stirs.  The hum of the engine is gone.  The chaos is gone.  The bus is still.  She blinks at the clock overhead.

**12:45 p.m.**

Twenty minutes of disorientation.  The kind of sleep that *ate time*.  She sits up slowly, hoodie falling back, hair a disaster.  And right there on the small table next to her bunk: **A brown paper bag.**  She sniffs.  **Whataburger.**

**TOM (O.S.)**
Figured you could use something to eat.

She turns. **Tom**, still in his driver’s seat, sipping bad coffee, eyes on the side mirror.

**TOM**
They all went into the Alamodome two hours ago.  Didn’t wanna wake you.

**(glances back)**
You’re awful skinny.

Kendall blinks, still fighting the fog, still holding the bag like it’s a sacred relic.

**KENDALL**
Did you…?

**TOM**
Yeah.  It’s got cheese.  I didn’t know what you wanted.  I just got the default.

**(beat)**
Eat it while it’s warm.

Kendall unwraps the burger slowly.  Takes one bite.  Closes her eyes.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I think I love this man.

---

## **EXT.  SERVICE LOT – OUTSIDE THE ALAMODOME – EARLY AFTERNOON**

Kendall steps off the tour bus, **burger in one hand**, hoodie shoved down, hair in that post-nap tangle that says *I survived something*.  She looks around.  And stops.  **It’s empty.**
Just a hot slab of Texas asphalt.  A cluster of buses lined like freight cars.  A few stagehands in the distance.  But no fans.  No vendors.  No humanity.  **And then—BOOM.**  The ground **rumbles** under her sneakers.  Not a tremor.  A *bass test*.  And then—**WHOOOOM.  WHOOOOM.**  A snare cracks like thunder in a vacuum.  She takes another step, shielding her eyes from the afternoon glare.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I’ve been to concerts.  I’ve been to stadium shows.  I’ve seen loud.

But this?

**(beat)**
This is *loud with no insulation.*  No crowds.  No bodies to absorb the punch.  No sweat, no denim, no plastic cups.Just ***130 decibels*** of uncut power, bouncing off steel and concrete.
And it makes the foundation of a 50,000-seat dome **shiver** like it’s afraid.  She walks closer to the rear entrance, burger still in hand, dumbstruck.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
This isn’t music.  This is physics.  And I think I just felt my *liver* vibrate.

---

## **EXT.  SERVICE LOT – NEAR DOME ACCESS DOOR – EARLY AFTERNOON**

Kendall edges closer to the structure, the low-end rumble now a **rolling earthquake** that seems to rearrange her bones every six seconds.  Suddenly—

**ROADIE (O.S.)**
First time hearing the dragon roar, huh?

She turns.  One of the **crew guys**, wearing a band tee faded into anonymity, waves from near the loading dock.  **He tosses something her way.**  Kendall catches it: a pair of padded earmuffs.  And then—protective goggles.  She stares at them.

**KENDALL**
Goggles?

**ROADIE**
You’re gonna need ‘em.

**(grinning)**
It gets real *flashy* in there when the lights sync with the punch.  Last guy walked in cold, puked behind the amp stacks and had a migraine for six hours.

**(beat)**
Welcome to *soundcheck*.

Another **sub-bass drop** hits, and Kendall stumbles half a step, catching herself on a rail.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Okay.  So this is what it feels like to join the cult of thunder.

She slides the earmuffs over her head.  Snaps the goggles into place.

**KENDALL**  (afraid)
Let’s do this.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – UNDERSTAGE CATACOMBS – MOMENTS LATER**

Kendall’s **goggles are pushed up on her head** now, earmuffs slung around her neck.  She’s walking carefully beneath the stage, her **Access All Areas** pass swinging gently from her lanyard.  The floor is a maze of **cables**, **flight cases**, and **the low murmur of technicians speaking in shorthand**.

**GUITAR TECH #1**
Capo 2, drop D, slide pre-set.

**GUITAR TECH #2**
Got it.  Tell him his Tele’s being weird again.

Kendall passes a **row of racks**, and then stops in front of a **setup that looks like a guitar armory**.  Twenty-four guitars.  All gleaming.  Some road-worn, some pristine. **Meticulously labeled.  Tuned.  Prepped.** Stratocasters.  Gretsches.  A couple of rare Gibsons that probably cost more than her grad school tuition.  She tilts her head.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Okay, that’s not a collection.  That’s a *manifesto*.

She glances at a clipboard hooked on the side of the rack.  The name is half-scribbled, but clear enough: **GILLEY.**

Kendall grins.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Of course.

She looks again at the array.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Gilley’s the kind of guy who would walk into a bedroom and have a guitar for every emotion he wants to fake.

She steps closer, one finger **not touching**—just tracing the air near the frets.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
And somehow…I don’t hate it.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – UNDERSTAGE – GUITAR TECH STATION – MOMENTS LATER**

Kendall’s still admiring the 24-guitar rack when a **crew member in a faded Slayer shirt and cargo shorts** leans over from behind a flight case.

**RANDALL ACKMAN**
Hey.  You got no idea how this works, do you?

Kendall straightens, caught off guard.

**KENDALL**
I mean… I know what a guitar looks like?

The tech jerks a thumb at the massive wall of instruments.

**RANDALL ACKMAN**
These 24?  They’re Jeremy’s.

He points across the space at a much smaller rack.

**RANDALL ACKMAN**
That one with two in it?  *That’s* Gilley’s.

**(smiling)**
Datdude delegates making music and preens for the womenfolk.

Kendall raises an eyebrow.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
He’s not wrong.  And he’s *chuffed* he gets to say it out loud.

She nods at the arsenal in front of her.

**KENDALL**
So this is the workhorse setup.

**RANDALL ACKMAN**
This is the cathedral.  Every guitar’s tuned, tested, mapped to a pedalboard and a set cue.  Jeremy could play a **funeral march in a thunderstorm** and still keep it tight.

He walks off with a coil of cables over one shoulder, whistling something in D minor.  Kendall turns back to the rack, properly humbled.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Okay.  Lesson learned.  *Respect the quiet ones.*

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – UNDERSTAGE – MOMENTS LATER**

Kendall watches the guitar tech disappear behind a rack, still impressed, still slightly rocked by the realization that **Jeremy is the sonic backbone**, not just a guy with a scowl and a tuner pedal.  She calls after him.

**KENDALL**
Hey—who are you?

The tech stops, glances back over his shoulder.  Narrow eyes under a sweat-stained baseball cap.

**RANDALL ACKMAN**
Name’s Randall Ackman.

**(beat)**
What’s it to ya?

Kendall raises her hands in mock surrender, grinning.

**KENDALL**
Just trying to learn the names of the people keeping this whole death machine running.  Randall shrugs, but there’s the faintest glimmer of satisfaction in his eyes.

**RANDALL**
Fair enough.

**(nods at the guitar rack)**
That one’s tuned for "Should I Press Pause?." If he breaks a string during the bridge, I’ve got 4.2 seconds to swap it or the whole night goes sideways.

He disappears back into the cables.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Okay.  Randall Ackman.  The man with 4.2 seconds to save the world.  Noted.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – UNDERSTAGE – CONTINUING**

Randall is checking over a patch cable when Kendall walks back over, coffee in one hand, burger long gone, brain fully engaged.

**KENDALL**
Hey, Randall.

He glances up, wary but polite.

**KENDALL**
When did you join the band?

He snorts.

**RANDALL**
’93.  Jer hired me in Dayton after their tech puked mid-show and I caught a falling Les Paul with one hand.

**KENDALL**
Damn.

**RANDALL**
Yup.

**KENDALL**
Where do you live?

**RANDALL**
Nominally?  Cincinnati.  Realistically?  Bunk five.

He shrugs toward the bus lot.

**KENDALL**
Where’d you go to school?

**RANDALL**
UC.  Mechanical engineering.  Dropped out.  This was louder.

She grins.

**KENDALL**
What do you love about the band?

Randall’s face actually softens, just a hair.

**RANDALL**
They don’t fake it.  They fight like hell.  But the music?  The music’s real.

**KENDALL**
You out partying and womanizing every night?

**RANDALL**
Nah.  I’m 44.  My knees don’t believe in afterparties.  Half the crew’s married.  Other half’s addicted to sleep.

He pulls a cable through a case groove like a man untangling a thought.

**KENDALL**
So what’s it like doing 190 shows a year?

Randall looks up, eyes sharp.

**RANDALL**
It’s a war.  A holy war.  You fight for the rhythm, for the gear, for the fans who scream like it’s their first concert and their last breath.

**(beat)**
Then you pack up, roll out, do it again.  That’s the job.

Kendall nods, quiet.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Okay.  That’s a story.

And maybe the beginning of a bigger one.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – UNDERSTAGE – CONTINUING**

Kendall watches Randall move with **unshakable confidence**, one hand coiling cable, the other balancing a guitar neck with surgeon-level steadiness.

**KENDALL**
You know you’re like… twice the age of the guy playing that guitar, right?

Randall doesn’t flinch.  Doesn’t even look up.

**RANDALL**
What’s it to ya?

**(beat)**
Takes a long time to get good at this.

He adjusts a tuning peg half a millimeter.  Plucks one string.  Repeats it.

**RANDALL**
I gotta hit the exact notes, with the exact tone,  at the exact moment Jeremy is thinking it.

**(beat)**
My job?  Is knowing what Jeremy’s gonna think *before he does*.

He finally looks at her, eyes sharp, voice even.

**RANDALL**
It’s like photocopying his brain.  Then summoning it—*perfectly*—on demand.  Tone, pitch, tempo, reverb, delay, preamp.  Every click, every pedal, every string tension.  All of it.

**(beat)**
I don’t just hand him guitars.  I hand him *miracles*.

He slides the guitar into a cradle and nods once.

**RANDALL**
That’s the work.

Kendall stares at him, momentarily stunned.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I have *so* much to learn.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – UNDERSTAGE – CONTINUING**

Kendall steps forward, eyes bright, voice tentative but serious.

**KENDALL**
Can I shadow you for a day?

Randall doesn’t even look up.

**RANDALL**
Yeah… no.  Not right now.

He lifts another guitar, tests the weight, adjusts the strap.

**RANDALL**
We’re in the **busy phase** now.  Curtain comes up in six hours, and I’ve got seven hours of work to do.

Kendall frowns.

**KENDALL**
How does that math even work?

Randall grins.

**RANDALL**
I skip bathroom breaks, mostly.

He nods toward the loading dock.

**RANDALL**
Pyro gets here in twenty.  Once that starts, I gotta duck out.  Safety protocols.  Union stuff.  Also, you know—*explosions*.

Kendall nods, fully absorbing it.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
This isn’t backstage.  It’s a damn battlefield.

**KENDALL**
When should I ask again?

Randall shrugs, measuring string tension like a man tuning a sniper rifle.

**RANDALL**
Try me tomorrow.  Morning’s best.  Before the chaos starts up again.

**(beat)**
I’ll know by 10 a.m.  if I’ve got time to teach you how to not trip over a DI box.

Kendall smiles.

**KENDALL**
Deal.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – SERVICE CORRIDOR NEAR PYRO STAGING – MOMENTS LATER**

Kendall’s curiosity gets the better of her.  She drifts toward the heavy black curtain marked *“CREW ONLY – PYRO STAGE PREP.”*

She’s one step away from peeking in when—

**BUBBA (O.S.)**
Ma’am.

She turns.

**BUBBA** stands beside the door like a slab of carved Appalachian granite. **6’4, full mustache, white crew cut, and a tour lanyard with SECURITY stamped in Helvetica.** He does not blink.

**BUBBA**
You are not allowed to go in there.

**(beat)**
If you persist in your actions, I will have to break you in half, snap you like a twig, and tie you around one of them bleachers like a ribbon on a church lady’s purse.

Kendall blinks.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
This man just threatened to make me into *accessorized kindling*.  In a **monotone**.

Bubba continues, voice **so calm it’s haunting**.

**BUBBA**
This is not a negotiation.  This is not sarcasm.  This is a formal warning in the interest of your physical safety.

**(beat)**
And mine.

Kendall slowly backs away.

**KENDALL**
Yes, sir.  Thank you, sir.

**(V.O.)**
What the *hell* kind of cowboy did I just meet?

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – CONCOURSE OUTER EDGE – MOMENTS LATER**

Kendall lingers nearby as Bubba keeps watch over the pyro staging corridor, arms crossed like two logs strapped to a wall.  She clears her throat.

**KENDALL**
Where’d you learn how to work with pyro?

Bubba doesn’t blink.  Doesn’t even shift his stance.

**BUBBA**
United States Army.

**(beat)**
I blew stuff up.

**(another beat)**
A lot of shit up.

**(slightly more solemn)**
EOD work.  Explosive Ordnance Disposal.

He glances at her, voice still flat as dry wheat.

**BUBBA**
It gave me nerves of steel.  And a healthy respect for pressure triggers.

Kendall nods slowly, brain trying to match his calm tone to the *apocalyptic stakes* of that résumé.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
This man is so dry he makes the Sahara look like a water park.

**(beat)**
No.  Atacama.  *Bubba is the Atacama Desert with a tour badge.*

She offers a nervous half-smile.

**KENDALL**
So…  this is your retirement gig?

**BUBBA**
No, ma’am.

**(beat)**
This is my upgrade.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – SERVICE HALLWAY – EARLY AFTERNOON**

Kendall walks briskly, eyes scanning lanyards, counting buses in her head, mentally cataloging gear crates and portable AC vents.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Six buses.  Not just for the band—*that’s* the trick.  How many of these people are *roadies*?  How many are *contractors*?  Who flies in?  Who lives on a bunk?  Who builds this whole beast from the bottom up, every city, every night?

She rounds a corner, looking for **Jim**.  Nothing.  Tries the green room hallway.  Empty.  Heads toward the floor-level concourse.  And there—**Cremeans.**

Clipboard in one hand, Bluetooth headset on, eyes locked on a schedule grid like its **battlefield intel**.

**KENDALL**
Hey.

He looks up, instantly reading her face.

**CREMEANS**
You’ve got a question.

**KENDALL**
How many people are on this crew?

He doesn’t blink.

**CREMEANS**
This leg?  Eighty-two full-time.  Twenty-six locals for rigging, thirteen more for load-out.  Pyro gets their own team.  Catering’s a separate contract.  Two buses for band.  One for management.  Three for crew.  Drivers rotate.  Everyone else rides hard.

Kendall’s jaw drops just slightly.

**KENDALL**
Eighty-two?

**CREMEANS**
And that’s just *our* side.  You wanna count union labor and venue hands, double it.  Triple it if we’re filming.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Jesus Christ.  I thought I joined a band.  I joined a *circus* with a payroll.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – SERVICE HALLWAY – CONTINUING**

Cremeans is already turning back to his clipboard when Kendall puts up a hand.

**KENDALL**
Wait a second—wait a second.  Hang with me here.

He pauses.

**KENDALL**
How many people in *your* shop are union?

**(tilts her head)**
Because I would’ve guessed zero.  You *reek* of Newt Gingrich.

Cremeans looks up slowly.  One eyebrow lifts.

**CREMEANS**
That’s adorable.  You think I’d let the AFL-CIO anywhere near my routing sheets.

**(beat)**
Zero.  Crew’s ours.  Direct hire, all at-will, all extremely well-paid.  If they want benefits, they can buy stock in the merch table.

Kendall just stares.

**KENDALL**
That’s the most libertarian thing I’ve heard since Rush Limbaugh said poor people should rent potholes to pay taxes.

**CREMEANS**
And yet here you are, riding on my tour bus for free.  Life’s pretty weird.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Jesus Christ.  I’m working for the Ayn Rand Marching Band.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – SERVICE HALLWAY – CONTINUING**

Kendall’s still reeling from his “no union” comment, lip curled in half-ironic disbelief.  Cremeans watches her, expression unreadable.  Then he shrugs.

**CREMEANS**
Before you get too fired up, let me clue you in—Every city we hit, we hire local union staff.  Lighting, rigging, cleanup, staging.

**(gestures vaguely upward toward the dome structure)**
For a venue like this?  Alamodome?  With these lighting arrays and this much weight in steel and cable?  You're looking at probably **fifty to sixty** union hands working today.

He steps in closer, clipboard still in hand.

**CREMEANS**
So let me ask you something, Kendall.

**(beat)**
How many people have you *ever* paid?

**(another beat)**
Have you ever met a payroll?  Ever *been* in a union?  Ever *hired* a union member?

**(beat)**
Better yet—have you ever sat down and had breakfast with one?

She opens her mouth.  Nothing comes out.  Cremeans doesn’t wait.

**CREMEANS**
I did.  This morning.

**(voice steady)**
Hotcakes and sausage with six of ’em.  Ironworkers, two electricians, a rigger, and a forklift guy named Marty who’s probably stronger than all of us put together.

**(grins faintly)**
Nice guys.  Good talkers.  Love their jobs.

He steps back.

**CREMEANS**
You want to write something real?  Start there.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – SERVICE HALLWAY – CONTINUING**

Kendall stares at Cremeans, eyes narrowed, lips tight.

**KENDALL**
Can I do that?

**(beat)**
Do I have creative control to actually write that kind of piece?

Cremeans doesn’t even flinch.

**CREMEANS**
If you keep it as a feature?

**(nods)**
Hell yes.

**(leaning in, tone shifting to sales pitch)**
The fans will *eat it up*.  Because then?  They don’t just see a band.  They see a *lifestyle*.

**(spreads arms)**
You too can grow up one day and join a traveling circus.  Tour strange American cities.  Play rock and roll so loud it breaks bones.  Live on a bus.  Breathe gasoline and feedback.

**(grins)**
And at the end of the night—if the gods smile on you?  You get to **screw the prom queen.**

Kendall stares at him, blinking slowly.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
God help me.  This man is marketing *the apocalypse* as an internship.

**KENDALL**
Okay.  Deal.  Let’s tell the truth.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – STAGE LEFT SERVICE AREA – NEAR CURTAIN – LATE AFTERNOON**

Kendall rounds a corner, and there he is.  **Jim.**  But not hotel Jim.  Not coffee-and-boxers Jim.  This is **stage Jim**.  **Blue jeans.  Leather vest.**    **Boots laced.**  **His shiny bald head dulled with powder to cut glare.** He’s standing near a case, not talking.  Not smiling.  **Just tapping.**  His drumsticks move in slow, twitchy patterns—**air snare, ghost kick, flick of a high hat.**  **Practicing nothing.  Practicing everything.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
That’s not the man who let me steal his coffee.  That’s the man who’s about to light a building on fire with rhythm.

She watches him quietly.  No one’s bothering him.  He’s not holding court.  He’s not posing.  **He’s gearing up.**  And the **nervous twitch in his wrists?** That’s the truth.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
This is the job.  And I get to see the man inside the suit of armor.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – STAGE LEFT – CONTINUING**

Kendall lingers near the rigging, watching Jim air-drum his way through invisible patterns.  She starts to step back, giving him space.  But before she can vanish—

**JIM**
HEY!

**(points a stick at her)**
Get your *sweet ass* over here!

Kendall blinks, caught like a deer in footlights.

**JIM**
Yeah, you!

**(drumstick still aimed like a wand)**
I got some *splainin’ to do.*

She walks over, ducking wires and stepping around a lighting rig.

**KENDALL**
You, uh… you look like you’re about to command a Viking longship.

**JIM**
That’s because I am.  Except instead of oars, I’ve got eight toms and a smoke cannon.

**(grins)**
You ready for the ride?

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – STAGE LEFT – CONTINUING**

Jim points a drumstick at Kendall’s chest—**not at her, but at her badge**.

**JIM**
That says *Access All Areas.*

**(taps it once)**
That means you can stick your nose into everything.

**(beat)**
But it’s a *judgment call*, alright?

Sometimes?  You don’t stick your dick—or your mic—just anywhere you want.

**(dead serious now)**
*Read the room.*  But don’t *shy away* either.  You’re getting paid.

Kendall opens her mouth, hesitates.

**KENDALL**
I… actually don’t know how much I’m getting paid.

Jim stops.

**JIM**
Wait, what?

**KENDALL**
We never really… discussed wages.  It just kind of—

**JIM**
Jesus Christ!

He puts both sticks down.  Points at her again, firmer now.

**JIM**
That’s why women shoot themselves in the foot.  They never think about the bottom line.

**(beat)**
There’s only two things in this world that matter—*Benjamins and pussy.*

**(points again)**
And you?  You only got *one* of ‘em.

Kendall raises an eyebrow.

**KENDALL**
Wanna bet?

Jim pauses.  A half-smile.  A half-acknowledgment.  He’s *testing* her—and she passed.

**JIM**
Alright.  We’re gonna fix that.  After the show—we talk numbers.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – STAGE LEFT – CONTINUING**

Kendall, arms crossed, tone icy.

**KENDALL**
Thanks for the chauvinism.

Jim doesn’t blink.  Just tilts his head, studies her like a case file.

**JIM**
Huh.

**(beat)**
You mean to tell me you took a job and didn’t even try to *lean in*?

Didn’t say up front— *“This is my bottom line.  If you can’t meet it, I walk.”*  Didn’t say— *“Here’s my worth.  Pay me or piss off.”*  Or did you just…**play along?  Get along?  Go along?**

**(steps closer, voice sharper)**
Is that what you did?  Did you stand up for yourself?  Or did you just slide right on in?

**(beat)**
*You* tell *me* who the chauvinist is.

Kendall’s breath catches—anger, embarrassment, something more complex.  Jim doesn’t let up.

**JIM**
There’s one person in this world who’s gonna take care of you, Kendall.

**(points at her chest again)**
And it’s **you**.  If you don’t do it?  That’s on you.

**(beat)**
Suffer.

He walks away, grabbing his sticks, back into performance mode.  Kendall stands there, eyes blazing.  Silent.  Processing.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Jesus H.  Christ.  This man doesn’t just bang drums.  He bangs *truth*.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – NEAR STAGE LEFT – MINUTES LATER**

Kendall sits alone on a road case, the sound of tuning amps and mic checks echoing in the distance.  Her badge still dangles against her chest.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Best paycheck I’ve ever seen?  Thirty-six grand.  Last year.  Thirty.  Six.  Thousand.

**(beat)**
Jim implied he made *nine and a half times that* in three months.  And that was **seven years ago**.

**(beat)**
No wonder my student loan balance hasn’t budged.  No wonder I’m here chasing someone else’s circus.

She watches as crew members hustle by, oblivious to her internal combustion.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Maybe the jerk doesn’t have much in the way of manners.  Maybe he’s all keyed up on adrenaline, about to go full Animal behind that kit.  Or maybe—just maybe—

**(beat)**
He laid down the *truth* like a goddamn flamethrower.

**(beat)**
Just like Tony *Montana*.  But bald.  And with less cocaine.

She exhales hard.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Okay, Jim.  You win this round.  But next time?  I come loaded.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – STAGE WING – MOMENTS BEFORE CURTAIN**

The roar of the crowd **builds like an earthquake**, shaking the rafters.  The **intro track** blares—**massive synth swells, programmed drums, distortion samples** layered thick and loud.  Kendall stands just offstage, half-sheltered by curtain rigging.  And then she sees them.  **All six members of Commuted**—racing toward each other in a tight huddle, like linebackers before the snap.  **Jim’s at the center.**  No mic.  No gear.  Just **pure fire in his eyes**, arms gesturing wildly, mouth moving fast.  She can’t hear him—can’t make out a word—but she can see it in his stance, in the way the others lean in:  **This is the war speech.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I can’t hear a damn thing.  But whatever he’s saying?  It’s got blood in it.

Then—

**JIM**  (visible, screaming)
**ONE.  TWO.  THREE.  FOUR!**

They all erupt—shouting, laughing, smacking palms.  **High fives all around.**  A final squeeze of shoulders.  A pat on the back.  The ritual complete.  The lights drop.  The **crowd detonates.**

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – STAGE WING – SECONDS AFTER CURTAIN DROP**

The lights go out.  The *intro track dies.*  And then—

**KATHY** steps to the mic and screams something guttural, **something primal**—  And the band detonates into their opener:

**"SWEET MEMORIES IN A DIVE BAR."**

**BOOM.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Oh.  Oh no.

**The bassline hits** like a car crash, rumbling through the soles of her boots and **into her spine**.  The guitars **snarl**, Kathy’s vocals **rip** the dome in half.  It takes exactly **two seconds** for Kendall to panic and slam the **earmuffs back over her ears.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
*This* is why they gave me the earmuffs.

Even muffled, the sound is **overwhelming**—not painful, not just loud—**Physical.**  Like someone **punched her lungs from the inside**.  **130 decibels.**  **Pure sonic force.**
Air *moves*.  Hair *lifts*.  Her jacket *ripples* like a flag in a storm.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
This isn’t music.  It’s *recreational warfare*.

And she’s inside the barricades.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – SERVICE AREA NEAR CRAFT TABLE – MID-SHOW**

Kendall’s ears are protected.  Her heart’s still **trying to settle into a normal rhythm** after the audio freight train of the opening track.  She ducks through a service hallway, just looking for **a moment to breathe**.  And then she sees it.  **Jeff Cremeans.**  Sitting alone at a **plastic folding table**, surrounded by warming trays and branded water bottles.  **He’s calmly eating Chinese food.**  A full plate: lo mein, General Tso’s, a spring roll like a cigar in one hand.  **Not even facing the stage.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
What the actual hell?

**(beat)**
They just blew out 50,000 sets of eardrums.  And the man running the whole damn machine?

**(beat)**
He’s on his *second egg roll.*

She watches him for a moment, stunned.  No phone.  No headset.  Just **noodles and silence**.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Why isn't he watching the show?  Doesn’t he care?  Isn’t this *his* symphony?  Or is this just… Tuesday?

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – CRAFT SERVICES AREA – MID-SHOW**

Kendall steps closer, flinching every time a bass kick rumbles the walls.  The music is **so loud** it feels like it’s in her teeth.  She half-shouts to be heard.

**KENDALL**
Jeff?!  Why aren’t you watching the show?

Cremeans calmly looks up, chews a bite of egg roll, dabs his mouth with a napkin like they’re at a quiet café in Vienna.

**CREMEANS**
My work is done here.

**(beat)**
I won’t be needed for another seventy-eight minutes.  Plus-minus ten seconds.

Kendall stares at him.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
What kind of supervillain schedules his disengagement time with *decimal accuracy*?

Cremeans forks some lo mein like he’s got **zero interest in the sonic war** unfolding a hundred feet away.

**CREMEANS**
They’re in good hands now.  The band’s tight.  Pyro’s queued.  Crowd’s committed.  No disasters inbound—yet.

**(glances at his watch)**
I’ll be back in place before the breakdown in “*County Fair Confession.*”  There’s a cue I might have to override if Kathy gets too wild.

He goes back to his food.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I have no idea whether I’m impressed or horrified.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – CRAFT SERVICES AREA – CONTINUING**

Cremeans pokes at his lo mein like it’s an equation.  Kendall is still hovering, confused, overwhelmed by the **contrast between the arena’s sonic Armageddon** and this **bizarre zen office breakroom vibe.**  She leans in closer.

**KENDALL**
So you're just… not involved?

**CREMEANS**
I don’t have anything to do with the music.

**(beat)**
That’s all on *them*.

He points toward the stage with a chopstick, casually, like it’s a minor footnote in his schedule.

**CREMEANS**
I’m just here to keep things down to a dull roar when they’re *not* on stage.

**(glances at watch again)**
When they’re in the zone like they are right about now?  Not my worry.

**(beat)**
I assume they’re going to kick butt and take names.  They usually do.

Kendall sits down across from him, still watching him like he’s a rare bird at a museum exhibit.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Okay.  This man isn’t a rock manager.  He’s a *storm bunker*.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – CRAFT SERVICES – CONTINUING**

Kendall leans forward slightly, elbows on the table.  The stage behind them is shaking with another track.  The crowd roars like a thunderstorm.

**KENDALL**
So… how much do I make?

Cremeans doesn’t look up.  He’s stirring rice with his fork.

**CREMEANS**
How much do *you* want to make?

Kendall blinks.

**KENDALL**
Wait, seriously?

**CREMEANS**
Dead serious.

**(finally looks up)**
You want a number from me?  I’ll give you a number.  But I’d rather hear your number first.

**(beat)**
Because if you can’t name your value, why should I?

Kendall swallows hard.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Jesus.  Jim drops truth like a sledgehammer.  Cremeans?  He sets the *trap* and lets you walk into it.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – CRAFT SERVICES – CONTINUING**

Kendall plants the number.

**KENDALL**
Seventy-five.  Base salary.  Plus travel comp.  Per diem in writing.  And I want rights to all my drafts—unless you buy them out, piece by piece.

Cremeans watches her for a beat.  Then—He nods.

**CREMEANS**
Done.

Kendall blinks, surprised by how easily it lands.

**CREMEANS**
I was willing to go to one-oh-five.

**(beat)**
But hey—*you* aimed low.

She stares.  Speechless.  Cremeans shrugs, casual as folding laundry.

**CREMEANS**
Next time, learn to negotiate.  And maybe next year when we revisit this?  You’ll do better.

He picks up his fork again.

**CREMEANS**
Everybody’s gotta learn sometime, Kendall.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – CRAFT SERVICES – MOMENTS LATER**

Cremeans is back to eating lo mein like nothing happened.  Kendall sits frozen, staring into space.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I just got exactly what I asked for.  On the first try.  And I thought I came in high.  But did I research market wages?  No.  Did I anchor the number with any leverage?  No.  I just threw out seventy-five like it was a **power move**.  And he said *yes* with chopsticks in his hand.

**(beat)**
Which means I aimed too low.

**CREMEANS (offhand)**
Fringe benefits too.  IP control.  Creative latitude.

He takes a sip of water.

**CREMEANS**
And we’ll revisit next year.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
*Revisit next year.*  So that means—I’ve got the job. *For a year.*  And next year, 1999…Maybe I don’t walk in like a baby duck waiting to get murdered.  Maybe I know my damn worth.  Maybe I ask for one-oh-five.  Maybe I ask for **more.**

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – CRAFT SERVICES – CONTINUING**

Cremeans finishes the last of his lo mein, wipes his mouth, and looks at Kendall like he’s just filed her.

**CREMEANS**
We’re private sector, Kendall.  You learn fast.  Or you get *run over*.

**(beat)**
Because we’re taxpayers.

**(leans forward slightly, not cruel—just honest)**
You might write real pretty.  But you’re *hopeless* when it comes to money.

He stands, tosses his napkin on the tray.

**CREMEANS**
Fix that.  Or don’t.  Your call.

He walks off, back into the belly of the dome.  Kendall sits alone for a moment, the roar of the band shaking the air.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Okay.  Lesson learned.  *Next time, I bring teeth.*

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – UNDERSTAGE – MID-SHOW**

Kendall slips down the corridor stairs, letting the seismic boom of the music above wash over her from a distance.  And underneath the stage—It’s like an *army ant convention*.  Fifteen people minimum.

- **Guitar techs swapping instruments like pit crew at a Formula One race.**
- **Electricians with radios and flashlights making last-second adjustments.**
- **Rigging operators tracking digital cues, timing platform lifts to fractions of a second.**
- **Cables.  Tools.  Quiet communication.  Tension everywhere.**

All of it invisible to the crowd.  All of it keeping the show from exploding—or collapsing.  Kendall stays low, out of the way, watching the orchestration with wide, quiet eyes.  And then she sees him.

**Bubba.**

Stationed against a support column, arms folded, watching her like **a border patrol agent guarding Valhalla.**  He doesn’t move.  Doesn’t speak.  Just watches.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
He’s not worried I’ll break anything.  He’s worried I’ll walk into something that breaks *me*.  And he’s probably right.

She nods once at him.  Bubba nods back.  Once.  Silent understanding.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – STAGE WING – END OF FIRST SET**

The band slides from chaos into control.  The lights drop to a moody low.  And then comes the unmistakable drum lead-in.

**“Why Her and Not Me?”**

Kendall freezes at stage right.  She knows this one.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
This is the one that cracked open the band’s second album.  The one with **two bridges**, a **fake outro**, and enough **seven o’clock confessions** to make every broken heart in the crowd look up and say *me too.*  Jim is locked in—**surgical, sweating**, not even blinking.  Every beat is **precise pain**.  Every pause is intentional.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
He *built* this.  Structured it like a flashback.  Like denial, followed by acceptance, followed by more denial.  And the fake ending?  That’s not a gimmick.  That’s the part where you think the heartbreak’s done.  And then it comes back.  Louder.  More honest.  More *real*.

The lights hit a gentle amber as the crowd **sings the outro back to the band**—And Jim, sweat dripping, eyes narrowed, just **rides the moment like a ghost riding thunder.**

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – BACKSTAGE SERVICE AREA – BETWEEN SETS**

The stage dims.  The crowd roars.  And the band?

**Explodes offstage.  Jim makes a beeline straight to the nearest porta-potty**, clutching his towel like a battlefield banner.  **Kathy is stripping off layers mid-run**, yelling for space.  The stage manager **throws up a makeshift modesty shield with two large black sheets**, one clipped to a mic stand, the other gripped tight by a terrified-looking assistant.  **Bill is already chugging water.  Gilley grabs two Gatorades and a banana.  Jeremy?  Blowing his nose repeatedly** into what might be his third tissue in thirty seconds.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I always wondered.  What do musicians *do* between sets?  Do they meditate?  Do they hug?  Do they toast champagne?

**(beat)**
Nope.  They **pee**, strip, sniffle, chug electrolytes, and try to *be human again* for six and a half minutes.

**(beat)**
It’s messy.  And kind of beautiful.  And maybe the most real thing I’ve seen all night.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – BACKSTAGE SERVICE ZONE – CONTINUING**

Kendall watches the madness swirl—Jim’s in a porta-potty, Kathy’s behind a privacy curtain, Gatorade bottles clink, techs race by with towels and clipboards.  Then—**a towel arcs through the air**.  She catches it on reflex.  Turns.  **Jeremy Gilley** is standing ten feet away, breathing hard, sweat gleaming off his collarbone, one Gatorade in hand, banana in the other.  He grins—**just a little.** Enough to register.  Enough to **charm and disarm**.

**GILLEY**
Hey.

Kendall stares for a beat.  He doesn’t follow up.  Doesn’t say anything else.  Just nods once, then turns and walks away, towel over his shoulder.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
That’s it?  No speech?  No flirtation?  No witty quip?  Just **hey**?

**(beat)**
Okay.  Cool.

**(beat)**
Maybe he’s not trying to seduce me.

**(beat)**
Maybe.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – BACKSTAGE SERVICE CORRIDOR – SECONDS LATER**

Kendall turns, towel still in hand.  She watches Jeremy Gilley disappear behind a curtain near the guitar racks.  Not fast.  Not dramatic.  Just *casual.*

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
That “Hey” wasn’t a move.  It wasn’t a line.  It was… *an opening.*  And maybe not even for anything big.  But curiosity?  Yeah.  That’s a powerful thing.

She follows.  Past rigging.  Past empty cases.  Past half-drunk sports drinks and printouts of the setlist taped to folding tables.  She peeks around the edge.  Gilley is **leaning over a guitar case**, towel draped over his neck, slowly running a cloth over the body of his backup Strat like it’s a ritual.  Not performing.  Not posing.  Just… decompressing.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
He’s not turned on.  He’s not turned out.  He’s just… *coming down.*  He looks up.  Sees her.  Doesn’t flinch.  Just smiles again.  Smaller this time.

**GILLEY**
You following me?

**KENDALL**
Just curious.

**GILLEY**
That’ll get you far around here.

He gestures to a folding chair.

**GILLEY**
Sit, if you want.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Okay.  Maybe “Hey” was the beginning of something, after all.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – GUITAR RACK ZONE – CONTINUING**

Kendall settles into the folding chair Jeremy Gilley pointed to.  She doesn’t ask anything.  Doesn’t take out her notebook.  She just sits.  Gilley keeps slowly wiping down the guitar.  Neck, bridge, pickups.  Polishing without urgency.  No one else around.  Just **hum from the stage**, faint **vibration from the crowd**, and a shared **pocket of stillness** under a stadium built for thunder.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I thought I’d have questions.  About the song.  About the show.  About how he plays like he’s trying to break the sky.  But now?  I don’t want to ask.  I just want to *be*.

Across from her, Gilley finishes the Strat.  Cradles it for a second like it’s an old pet.  Then he sets it gently back in the case.  No words.  Just a nod.  A little one.  Like he’s saying *thanks for letting the moment be what it was.*  She nods back.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
No flirting.  No revelations.  No angles.  Just breath.  Just sweat.  Just…  space.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – GUITAR RACK ZONE – CONTINUING**

Gilley gently closes the guitar case.  He glances over at Kendall, his expression unreadable—Then says, quietly:

**GILLEY**
Touching.

And in a flash—he **leaps to his feet**, **clicks his heels midair like a cartoon soldier**, and sprints off down the hallway, laughing to himself.  Kendall watches, stunned.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
What the hell was that?  Was that… *joy?*

She peers out from behind the curtain.  Gilley rejoins the other four band members near the service corridor.  **Bill's stretching.  Jim's towel-whipping his forearm.  Jeff’s retuning something by ear.**  They’re all waiting.  **One missing.**  Kathy.  Still behind her makeshift curtain.  Still mid-change.  Kendall grins.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Five on deck.  One diva to go.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – BACKSTAGE SERVICE AREA – MOMENTS LATER**

The band is huddled again—five strong—waiting, buzzing, pacing.  And then—**Kathy emerges.**  Not walks—*emerges*.  **Black velvet corset, heels like daggers, legs for days.  Epic cleavage.**  **Black lipstick.  Hair pinned like she’s about to drain a nobleman.**  It’s **gothic.  Erotic.  Stage-ready.  Weaponized.**  Kendall freezes mid-step.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Oh my *god*.  This isn’t just a second set.  This is a **reincarnation**.  She looks like she just killed a Victorian duke for his estate and kept the title.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
That’s not a wardrobe change.  That’s a *transformation*.  *Vampire.  Seductress.  Power incarnate.*  You've got to be kidding me.

Kathy walks straight past Kendall without a glance, eyes locked on the curtain.  **All sex.  All fury.  All fire.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
This is *surreal.*

And it’s only halfway through the night.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – SIDE STAGE – TRANSITION TO SECOND SET**

Kendall stands tucked into the shadows, her notebook forgotten in her hand.  **Kathy and Gilley** brush past her—both radiant, both electric.  They **bump hips** in passing—light, flirtatious, a **mimicked kiss** made of rhythm and history.  They don’t even look at each other.  They don’t have to.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
It wasn’t staged.  It wasn’t for the cameras.  It was… *real*.  Like two people who’ve spent half their lives stealing moments in green rooms and stage wings.  Then—**Bill steps up.**  e strides toward the stairs with the cool confidence of a man walking into a storm he helped design.

**The house lights go down.**  A heartbeat of silence.  Then—**The crowd roars.**  Like the roof’s about to tear off.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
This isn’t act two.  This is *part two* of something *so much bigger*.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – STAGE WING – MINUTES INTO SECOND SET**

The crowd is already in a trance.  But then comes the **first chord** of *Should I Press Pause*—**A wave of fuzzed-out reverb**, thick as molasses, rolls across the dome like a sandstorm.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
What even is this?  Tom Petty got high in the Mojave Desert and handed his soul to a soundcheck from Mars?

Jeremy steps forward into the light, guitar slung low, **face dead serious, eyes closed**.  And then—**he lets it rip.**  **Bends.  Slides.  Whispers.  Screams.**  It’s not a solo.  It’s a **ritual**.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
He’s got complete control.  Of the room.  Of the band.  Of the *air*.  And it’s a room the size of a **small lake**.

Off to the side, **Bill hits the gong.** Once.  The vibration shudders through the floor.  Then again.  Then again.  Every few seconds, **a low-frequency prayer.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
They’re not just playing.  They’re *searching*.  For something holy.  Or stoned.  Or both.  Does this lead to Zen?  Maybe.  Maybe it already did.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – UNDERSTAGE & STAGE WING – MIDWAY THROUGH SECOND SET**

The band rips through track after track.  Gilley’s voice echoes above—throwing out a **quippy aside**, a **shouted joke**, a **flirtatious “How we doin’, San Antonio?”** between numbers.

**To the crowd:** It’s spontaneous.  It’s sexy.  It’s cool.  But Kendall?

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
What’s more fascinating than what’s *on* stage…Is what’s *beneath* it.  Every time Gilley talks for more than ten seconds—**cables move.  Pedals swap.  Guitar techs race to swap tunings.**  Light cues change.  It’s like watching **a pit crew choreograph themselves around a song.**  But if there’s no break—if the band bleeds straight into the next track?

**Nothing happens.**  The people under the stage go still.  **Frozen.**  

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Gilley knows.  Down to the *second*.  He knows **exactly** how long the crew needs to swap gear.  Repatch a signal.  Reboot a loop station.  And he gives it to them.  It *sounds* like ad-libbing.  But it’s not.  It’s **blueprinted**.  **Sketched.  Timed.  Executed.**  A script made to sound like a heartbeat.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – UNDERSTAGE CORNER – CONTINUING**

Kendall hunches down on a crate near a gear rack.  **Notebook open.  Pen a blur.**  She’s not writing articles—**she’s planting dynamite.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
There’s too much.

It’s not chaos—it’s *precision on fast forward.*

**Scrawled notes fly across the page:**

- *Gilley \= human metronome for road crew?*
- *Jeremy’s heel-click: charisma or code?*
- *Bubba as guardian / dry philosopher.  TV show in disguise?*
- *Kathy \= Act I goddess, Act II vampire.  Who decides the transformation schedule?*
- *Guitar techs — IDENTICAL routines, yet every swap is different… why?*
- *Jeff Cremeans eating egg roll while 50,000 people scream.  Must ask: is detachment a performance too?*

She glances back up, eyes wild, hair sticking to her temple.

**Another line:**

- *This tour isn’t music. It’s physics.  Sociology.  Porn.  Ballet.  Logistics.*

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I came here to write one story.  I’ve got **thirty.**  And they’re *all happening at once.*

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – SIDE STAGE – NEARING THE FINAL ACT**

Kendall catches the setlist taped to the floor just outside the wings.  Her eyes scroll down.  And there it is.

***“Come Inside Me.”***

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Everyone loves the music that hit them at 18.  Because it feels like *everything*.  Like a secret written just for you.  And this one?  This was *mine*. 

She grips her notebook tighter.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Twelve minutes of raw power.  Synth sex.  Poetic profanity.  But—Where are the backup singers?

She looks around.  Nothing.  No one.

No women in sequins.  No backup mic stands.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
The 1991 recording had harmonies.  Had fire.  Had voices wrapping around Kathy like velvet rope.  But now?

**The synth loop hits.**  Low.  Icy.  Pulsing.  **Then Jim drops in—first on drum machine, precision-perfect, then live, organic fills layered over the track.  Then—Kathy.**  She **launches** into the first verse like she’s possessed by every heartbreak and orgasm of the 90s.  **Alone.**  Unrelenting.  Untouchable.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
They’re not recreating it.  They’re *reclaiming* it.  Rewriting it.  Stripped down.  Amplified.  It’s dirtier.  It’s angrier.  It’s *better*.  And it’s *still mine*.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – SIDE STAGE – DURING “COME INSIDE ME”**

The synth pulses on.  Kathy commands the spotlight.  But Kendall leans toward a nearby tech—**a woman in cargo shorts and a headset, hair pulled back tight.**

**KENDALL**
Where are the backup singers?  Why’s this version so stripped down?

The tech doesn’t look away from the stage.  Just grins.

**TECH**
Kathy chased ’em off.  After the second tour.

**KENDALL**
Seriously?

**TECH**
Couldn’t stand the idea of competition.  Not vocal. *Sexual.*

**(beat)**
Always thought someone was gunning for Gilley.  Or Jeff.  Or Bill.  Or Jim.  Or some… *cocktail combo* of the above.

**KENDALL**
Jesus.

**TECH**
Look—these guys?  They get around.  It’s not *not* justified.  But Kathy?  She’s territorial.  You sing behind her, you better not flirt in front of her.  Not if you wanna keep your gig.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
And here I thought it was an artistic choice.

**(beat)**
Turns out, it was just… *survival*.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – SIDE STAGE – “COME INSIDE ME” CONTINUING**

Kathy prowls the stage like a panther.  The crowd is losing their minds.  But Kendall?  She stands still.  Pen paused.  The tech’s words still hanging in the air.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Never meet your heroes.  Even your feminist ones.  Because they’re flawed.  Terribly.  Sometimes *ugly* in ways you don’t want to believe.

Kathy—
*Queen of the Anti-Patriarchy Anthem,*slayer of PMRC censors, playmate in Playboy, voice like a banshee with a PhD—**Kicked women off her own tour.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Not because they were bad.  But because they were beautiful.  Or maybe just confident.  And it threatened her.

**(beat)**
And somehow… that makes her feel more real.  More dangerous.  More *alive*.  But it also makes her…*mortal.*

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – STAGE WING – MOMENTS LATER**

Kathy’s voice echoes through the last line—**raw, ragged, godlike:**

**KATHY (ON MIC)**
*A tightening grip…*
*Let it go—*

**BOOM.**

**Flames erupt—forty feet high.**

**The crowd goes nuclear.**

**GILLEY (SCREAMING)**
***GOODNIGHT TEXAS!  WE'LL SEE YOU IN EL PASO!***

**And then—**  One by one—**They sprint offstage.  Kathy first—grinning, vibrating, her chest heaving.**  **Jim right behind her—sticks still in hand, shirt *completely* soaked.**  **Bill laughing like a lunatic.  Jeff with a towel already over his head.  Jeremy—arms raised, whooping, winded but grinning.**  They race down the back stairs like **warriors returning from battle.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
If they were high after the first set—Now?  They’re *exalted.*  Drenched in sweat.  Eyes lit like kids on Christmas.  **And every one of them—Beaming.**

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – SERVICE CORRIDORS – IMMEDIATELY AFTER SHOW**

Kendall hustles.  **Notebook in her back pocket.  Pen in her hand.  Eyes wide.**  She follows the trail—**sweaty towels, Gatorade bottles, roadies yelling directions, techs hauling racks.  Band members scatter** into different directions—still high on adrenaline.  **Jim’s headed for a cooler and a chair.  Kathy’s headed for the shower.  Gilley?  Nowhere visible.  Already vanished.**  She follows the **loudest voice**—probably Bill, who’s talking to no one and everyone.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
What do they do after they shatter a dome?  Pop champagne?  Do shots?  Smoke cigars and make out with roadies?  

She cuts through the curtain—And finds:

- **A cooler.**
- **A couple of couches.**
- **A massage table.**
- **Four fans.**

- **Cremeans with a clipboard.**
- **A production assistant with warm towels.**
- **A physical therapist kneeling at Jeff’s legs.**

And five band members—**Utterly spent.  Slouched.  Smiling.  Breathing.**  No speeches.  No high-fives.  No hype.  **Just decompression.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
They don’t celebrate.  They *land*.  Like astronauts re-entering Earth’s gravity.  And for the first time tonight—**They’re quiet.**

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – LOCKER ROOM – POST-SHOW**

The roar of the crowd is gone.  The fluorescent lights buzz faintly.  Kendall walks past rows of lockers, towels, a few abandoned setlists taped to benches.  
She hears water.

**Turns the corner—** And there’s **Kathy. Nude.  Kneeling.  Hunched.**  In the center of the **group shower**, arms draped over her knees, hair soaked and plastered to her neck and back.  Water streams over her shoulders like a **baptism and a punishment**.  She doesn’t see Kendall.  Or maybe she does, and just **doesn’t care**.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I came looking for the goddess.  I found the *wreckage of one*.  Not destroyed.  Just… **spent.**  Like the stage drained her.  Like every lyric had to be paid for in sweat and silence.

**KENDALL (softly)**
Kathy?

Kathy doesn’t move.  Then—quietly, hoarsely—

**KATHY**
Give me a minute.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Yeah.  Okay.  Take all the minutes you need.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – LOCKER ROOM – CONTINUING**

The steam gathers, dense and hot.  Kendall waits near the doorway, perched on a bench.  Quiet.  Still.  In the shower—**Kathy hasn’t moved.**  Ten full minutes pass.  She kneels, bare, water **sluicing over her**.  Hair like **black satin ropes**, clinging to her spine.  Skin like **alabaster**, drained and pale in the harsh fluorescent wash.  No glamour.  No angles.  No pose.  Just gravity.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
She’s not sexy.  She’s not mystical.  She’s not a goddess.  Not right now.  She’s a woman whose body just moved **a hundred thousand watts** of emotion through forty thousand screaming strangers.  And now?  Now she just lets the water **take what’s left.**

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – LOCKER ROOM – CONTINUING**

Kathy finally moves.  Slowly.  Stiffly.  She rises to her feet, slick with water, breathing deep.  Her body **creaks** like a machine that’s gone too long at redline.  She steps carefully out of the shower, eyes scanning the room.

**KATHY (grumbling)**
Where the hell is my towel?

Her eyes land on the costume—**a black heap of soaked velvet, latex, and mesh**, limp and exhausted on a nearby bench.  She frowns at it.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
That thing made her a vampire goddess an hour ago.  Now it just looks like it smells like a bar fight.  

Kathy bends—her back and **bare buttocks** streaked with **angry red indentations**, the ghost marks of the **corset that clung to her for eighty minutes** under lights and heat.  She winces.  Still no towel in sight.

**KATHY (to no one)**
Goddamn production team…

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – LOCKER ROOM – MOMENTS LATER**

Kendall spots it—**a towel**, folded over the edge of a supply cart.  She grabs it.  Hurries back.

**KENDALL**
It’s small.  But it’s something.

Kathy takes it wordlessly.  She presses it to her face first. **Lets it soak the steam.** Then to her shoulders.  Her arms.  Down her back.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
It won’t wrap.  Won’t cover.  But it dries.  And maybe that’s enough.

Kathy doesn’t thank her.  Doesn’t speak.  She just keeps drying.  Like **ritual.  Like recovery.  Like control returning.**  

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
This isn’t a post-show glam squad.  This is **battlefield medicine**.  Done solo.  And I just handed her the gauze.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – LOCKER ROOM – CONTINUING**

Kathy towels off, still hunched slightly, red marks along her ribs, thighs, back.  She doesn’t look up when she speaks.

**KATHY**
Can you get wardrobe down here?  I need a change.  They’ve got my sizes.

**(beat)**
I’ve already been seen naked by too many people tonight.

**(finally looks at Kendall)**
What’s one more?

Her voice isn’t bitter.  Just flat.  Honest.  Kendall nods.  No jokes.  No commentary.

**KENDALL**
Yeah.  I’ll find them.

She turns, heading for the hallway.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Kathy didn’t ask for privacy.  She asked for help.  And for once?  I knew exactly how to give it.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – SERVICE CORRIDORS – MOMENTS LATER**

Kendall steps out of the locker room.  And **boom**—she walks into a **different world.**  **Techs are hauling gear.  Crates are slamming shut.**  **Laughter bursts from down the corridor.**  Someone's blasting **Beastie Boys** from a Bluetooth speaker.  A group of crew members are **sharing beers**, collapsing into camp chairs.  **One guy lights a joint.** Passes it without a word.  **The smell rolls over her—skunky, sweet, and wild.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Inside the locker room: steam and silence.  Out here?  **A tornado made of giddy exhaustion.**  Half the crew is **still working like it’s a deadline**.  The other half is **partying like it’s a wrap party**.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
This is the engine.  **Pack.  Roll.  Drive.  Play.  Burn.  Repeat.**  And it never stops.  Not even for Kathy.

---

## **EXT.  ALAMODOME – LOADING DOCK – MOMENTS LATER**

Kendall rounds a corner and sees them—**Wardrobe crew** in black shirts and bandanas, **tossing armfuls of fabric, latex, leather, and mesh** into rolling bins.  The bins are ramped into the back of a **white Ryder truck**, hastily branded with a taped-on sign that says: **“WARDROBE 2 – DO NOT STACK GILLEY’S PANTS”**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
And there it is.  Not a boutique.  Not a trailer.  **A converted truck.** Like for moving apartments.  **Holding a thousand shows’ worth of sweat and sequins.**  Everything gets **stuffed, zipped, racked, binned.**  Because they’ve got **six hours to get on the road.**  El Paso waits.  The circus rolls on.

**KENDALL (calls out)**
I need Kathy’s backup change.

One of the crew tosses her a labeled bag from a bench seat.

**CREW GUY**
Tell her next time not to disappear naked.

**KENDALL**
Noted.

She takes the bag.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Pack it up.  Roll it on.  Repeat.  This is what **immortality looks like** in motion.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – SPURS LOCKER ROOM – MOMENTS LATER**

Kendall pushes the door open quietly.

Inside: dim light, soft hum of distant fans, faint reverb of the show still echoing in her bones.

She sees her:

**Kathy.**

**Asleep.**

Stretched **languidly** across a **leather recliner built for a seven-foot-tall man**, tucked into one of the San Antonio Spurs’ vacant locker stalls.

No personal effects.  No jersey.  No glam.

Just **leather.**

And **a rock goddess**, **naked**, curled up like a **well-fed cat**.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
She doesn’t need a bed.

She doesn’t need a dressing room.

She found comfort in the weirdest corner of a sports palace—
and now she looks like a **content pea in a pod.**

Kendall sets the wardrobe bag quietly on a bench nearby.

She doesn’t say a word.

She just watches Kathy breathe.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Stage devours her.
Water strips her.
And this chair?

This chair *restores* her.

## **INT.  SPURS LOCKER ROOM – CONTINUING**

Kendall crouches beside the wardrobe bag.

She unzips it—quietly, carefully—like it’s sacred.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Clean set.
Plain white tee.
Pink slacks.
Simple bra.  Matching panties.

**She checks tags: size six.  Bra: 34C.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Thirty-four C?

Huh.

She looks over at Kathy, still asleep, limbs tangled like a goddess after battle.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Looks bigger than that when she’s nude.

Maybe because she’s not just skin and bone.

She’s **stage and power and posture and smoke**.

She’s *larger than life*.
Even when she looks like hell.

She zips the bag shut and sets it gently beside the chair.

Then she slips out—silent, shoes barely scuffing the floor.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Okay.

Let her sleep.

The goddess gets to rest, too.

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – INTERIOR CORRIDORS – LATE NIGHT**

Kendall walks fast.

Then slower.

Then stops.

**Concrete walls.  Forking hallways.  Zero signage that makes sense.**

No band members.
No familiar voices.

Just **the hum of vents**, the **distant clank of crates**, the **sharp laughter of roadies somewhere else entirely**.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Jesus, this place is a maze.

I’ve been running for hours.
Locker room to stage.
Stage to trucks.
Back again.

Chasing towels.
Tracking clothes.
Watching gods fall asleep in basketball chairs.

**(beat)**
And I haven’t seen *Jim*.
Or *any* of them.

Where the hell do rock stars even go when the show’s over?

Do they have some **private offstage dimension** the rest of us can’t access?

She leans against the wall.

Breathes.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Okay.

Reset.
Recharge.
Find Jim.
Find air.

*Find the way out.*

---

## **INT.  ALAMODOME – EXIT CORRIDOR – CONTINUING**

Kendall hears it before she sees it—

**Laughter.**
**Metal clinks.**
**A *sizzle*.**
**Music from a Bluetooth speaker.**

She turns the corner—

And there it is.

**The loading dock.**

**Floodlit.  Loud.  Beautiful.**

Someone’s **wheeled out a full-size grill**—charcoal, not gas.

**Smoke curling into the Texas night.**
**Crew members lounging on amp cases.**
**Plastic cups and beer cans scattered like breadcrumbs.**
**Brats on the flame.  Burgers being flipped with a guitar pick.**

One guy’s **grilling shirtless**.  Another’s **using a kick drum as a table.**

It’s **chaos**, but it’s **homegrown**.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Oh my god.

They’re actually **grilling**.

On the *back dock*.

After setting 130 decibels on fire and vaporizing a dome—

They’re *tailgating.*

And it’s **perfect**.

---

## **EXT.  ALAMODOME – BACK DOCK – CONTINUING**

Kendall steps into the smoke and neon of the makeshift grill-up.

She scans the scene—

And there he is.

**Jeremy Gilley.**

**Leaned against a steel railing**, paper plate balanced precariously on a snare case.

**Hotdog in one hand.**
**A plain, boiled potato** in the other—skin on, no butter, no salt.

He bites it like it’s an apple.

Eyes half-lidded.  Sweaty.  Barefoot.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
There he is.

Jeremy fucking Gilley.

Last seen shredding the sky open like a preacher on acid.

Now?

Now he’s double-fisting **processed meat** and a **potato** like it’s **the last supper**.

He catches her watching.

Raises the potato.

**GILLEY**
You hungry?

## **EXT.  ALAMODOME – BACK DOCK – MOMENTS LATER**

Kendall’s stomach growls.

**Loud.**
Embarrassingly loud.

She eyes the grill.

**Grease popping.**
**Meat hissing.**
**The air thick with smoke and salt and sin.**

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
It’s 11:30 p.m.

My feet hurt.

My brain’s fried.

I’ve seen a goddess naked.  Twice.

And this?

This smells like **a holy crime.**

She walks toward the grill, eyes locked on a **double-patty cheeseburger** being flipped like a blessing.

Behind her, Gilley bites the last of his potato.

**GILLEY (casually)**
Told you.

She grabs a plate.

**KENDALL**
Give me the most depraved thing you’ve got.

**GRILL GUY**
Bacon-wrapped bratwurst with two slices of cheddar and shame?

**KENDALL**
Perfect.

## **EXT.  ALAMODOME – BACK DOCK – MOMENTS LATER**

Kendall settles onto an overturned road case beside Gilley.

He tosses his empty paper plate into a trash bin with a casual flick.

**GILLEY**
You ever do something for three hours so hard that you forget to breathe?

He doesn’t wait for an answer.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
We hit it at seven.  I don’t think I stopped moving till, what—ten fifteen?

**(laughs, low and loose)**
It’s like I black out somewhere in the third song, and when I wake up, I’ve sweat through my third shirt and my shoes are missing.

He gestures vaguely to his **bare feet**.

**GILLEY**
Crushingly crazy good night.

I think I levitated.

**(beat)**
Or had a stroke.  Honestly, could go either way.

He glances sideways at Kendall.

**GILLEY**
You look like someone who just saw how the sausage gets made.

**KENDALL**
I saw the sausage.  I *smelled* the sausage.  I nearly proposed to it.

They both laugh.  Quiet.  Exhausted.

But **real.**

## **EXT.  ALAMODOME – BACK DOCK – CONTINUING**

Gilley leans back, cracking open a fresh beer.

**GILLEY**
My post-levitation ritual?

**(grins)**
Food.
Beer.
Women.

**(beat)**
Usually in that order.  But not always.  Depends on the city.

He takes a sip, then eyes Kendall’s burger.

**GILLEY**
Tonight, though?

Might just stick with the first two.

I’m sweaty, half-dead, and I’ve got potato starch in my sinuses.

**(beat)**
Romance can wait.

## **EXT.  ALAMODOME – BACK DOCK – CONTINUING**

Gilley wipes his hands on a napkin, tosses it onto his empty plate.

**GILLEY**
I’m a shark.

**KENDALL**
Excuse me?

**GILLEY**
Shark.  Always swimming.  Even when I’m sleeping.

**(beat, glances toward the empty dome)**
If I stop moving?

I sink.

He says it light, like a joke.  But something about it **sticks**.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
I believe him.

Even now, feet bare, beer in hand, belly full—

**He’s still turning circles.**
**Just… slower ones.**

## **EXT.  ALAMODOME – BACK DOCK – CONTINUING**

Kendall grins.

**KENDALL**
So what happens when a shark falls in love?

Gilley doesn't blink.

**GILLEY**
Def Leppard said it best.

**(leans in, mock-serious)**
*Don’t need love,*
*Don’t need affection.*

**(grins)**
Look it up sometime.  Pyromania.  Peak shit.

He leans back against the case, stretches his arms, beer hanging from his fingers.

**GILLEY**
We opened for ’em.  Six years ago.  Tiny stage.  Cheap lights.  No pyro.  But I would’ve played *naked in the parking lot* just to be near them.

**(beat)**
Now look at us.

**(nods toward the dome)**
We’ve got more firepower than they ever did.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
And he says it not with arrogance.

But with… **gratitude.**  Like a shark who remembers *every single swim* on the way up.

---

## **EXT.  ALAMODOME – BACK DOCK – CONTINUING**

Gilley stares out into the night.

Quiet.  Then—

**GILLEY**
You know the best I ever had it?

Kendall looks over.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Glastonbury stop.  Last summer.

**(beat)**
We go on at 3 a.m.  GMT.  It’s cold, damp, people should’ve been crashing.

But no.

**(beat)**
It’s me, Bill, and Jeff.

Rhythm section locked the fuck in.

**KENDALL**
What were you playing?

**GILLEY (grinning)**
*Come Inside Me.*  We started the riff and… Jesus.  **It was like a hundred thousand people all caught the same seizure at once.**  Bass.  Drum fills.  Simple drone.  That’s all it took.

And then—

**(quietly)**
We nearly made a hundred thousand people come.  In public.

He laughs, shaking his head like he still doesn’t believe it.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I was in awe.  I wasn’t even *in* the band at that moment.  I was just… *inside someone wet.*

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Not sex.  Not power.  Just… **pure music.**  Pure motion.  Pure surrender.

---

## **EXT.  ALAMODOME – BACK DOCK – CONTINUING**

Kendall tilts her head, arching an eyebrow.

**KENDALL**
Has anything ever topped that?

Gilley doesn’t miss a beat.

**GILLEY**
Yeah.  But it’s not usually on stage.  It’s, uh—

**(grins, shameless)**
Usually backstage.  After.  You know.  Directly after.

**(beat)**
You should try it sometime.  It’s… *primal.*

**KENDALL**
Primal?

**GILLEY**
Post-concert hookups?  You’re high on adrenaline, soaked in sound, lit from the inside out.  It’s not romance.  It’s not flirting.  It’s like…

**(he gestures vaguely)**
Ritual.  Catharsis.  Sometimes…  revelation.

He finishes his beer.

**GILLEY**
No better time to hook up with someone.

---

## **EXT.  ALAMODOME – BACK DOCK – CONTINUING**

Kendall grins, leaning back with her burger.

**KENDALL**
Is that an offer or a sermon?

Gilley's grin widens.

**GILLEY**
Both.  But mostly?

**(shrugs, casual)**
Suggestion.  You should try it sometime.

**(beat)**
Works best in the summer, though.

**KENDALL**
Why summer?

**GILLEY**
Long nights.  Less clothing.  Sweat feels like holy water.

**(beat)**
And no one asks questions when you wander out barefoot at dawn looking like you survived a thunderstorm.

**KENDALL (V.O.)**
Jesus.  The man could bottle this.

---

## **EXT.  ALAMODOME – BACK DOCK – CONTINUING**

Kendall licks the grease from her thumb, eyes narrowing just slightly.

**KENDALL**
So what you’re saying is—If I time it right, wear the right clothes, and let the sweat do the talking—I might just find God?

**(beat)**
Or your bed?

Gilley stares at her, momentarily stunned.  Then—laughs.  Full-throated, eyes flashing.

**GILLEY**
Damn.  You don’t bluff, do you?

**KENDALL (shrugging)**
I don’t play if I’m not holding cards.

---

## **EXT.  ALAMODOME – BACK DOCK – LATER**

The banter eases into a **slow grin between bites and sips.**  Gilley wipes his mouth with the back of his hand, gazes off at the dome.

**GILLEY**
You know—You hang around here long enough, you start to realize something: I’m just the cocktail straw.

**KENDALL**
Excuse me?

**GILLEY**
Yeah.  I swirl the drink.  I make a lot of noise.  People remember the umbrella and the garnish—But the real flavor?

**(gestures with his bottle)**
That’s Jeff’s brain.  That’s Jim’s backbeat.  That’s Kathy’s madness.  That’s Bill’s wizardry.  Hell, even Jeremy’s got heat for days.

**(grinning)**
I just move things around and flash a little teeth.

**KENDALL**
You really believe that?

**GILLEY**
I believe we’re all indispensable.  But I also believe **I’m not the genius**.  I’m the gravity.  The flirt.  The spark.  

**(beat)**
And I’m good with that.

---

## **EXT.  ALAMODOME – BACK DOCK – CONTINUING**

Kendall leans forward, resting her elbows on her knees.

**KENDALL**
Bullshit.

Gilley raises an eyebrow, amused.

**KENDALL (CONT’D)**
You’re not a cocktail straw.

**(beat)**
You’re the eye of the hurricane.  Everything spins around you.  *You* dictate the energy.  You give the crew time with banter.  You whip 40,000 people into heat with a raised eyebrow.  You may not write every note, but don’t pretend like you don’t know what power feels like.

Gilley doesn’t blink.  Then—**he smiles.  A slow, tired, grateful smile.**

**GILLEY**
You see everything, don’t you?

**KENDALL**
I write it down.

---

## **EXT.  ALAMODOME – BACK DOCK – CONTINUING**

Gilley takes a long sip of beer, eyes twinkling in the fading light.

**GILLEY**
It’s all instinct.  All day.  Zero sense of planning.  Couldn’t choreograph a set if my life depended on it.

**(beat)**
I just… watch.  Listen.  Feel where the room is leaning.  And then I pounce.

**KENDALL**
Like a shark.

**GILLEY**

## **INT.  HOTEL ROOM – QUIET INTERIOR MONOLOGUE**

Kendall’s back is half to the mirror.  She’s sliding on her bra slowly, but her mind isn’t on her hands.  She replays it in her head.

## **INT.  HOTEL HALLWAY – MORNING**

The bags are packed.  The room key’s left on the dresser.  And Kendall walks like she’s **setting tempo**—a steady, intentional stride.  Jim lags half a step behind, pulling one bag, sipping lukewarm coffee from a paper cup.  They hit the elevator.  Then the lobby.  Then the loading zone.

And there it is.  **The tour bus.**  Waiting.  Engine low.  Doors open.  And **all six pairs of eyes are on them**—from inside, from steps, from behind sunglasses and morning scowls.

Gilley grins first.

**GILLEY (calling out)**
Daaaamn, Red.  You took him *hostage* or what?

The moment Kendall and Jim step through the door, **a bag of peanuts sails through the air** and bounces harmlessly off Jim’s chest.

## **INT.  TOUR BUS – LOUNGE – LATE MORNING**

Kendall curls into her corner of the wraparound booth, knees up, journal in her lap.  Headphones on, pencil in hand, she **doesn’t even need music**—just the motion of the road and the low hum of the bus.  Her mind’s racing.  Her fingers are trying to keep up.

She flips to a clean page and starts a quick **brain-dump list**:

- *Why do I feel more feminine after someone saw me as whole?*
- *Why does Kathy command thousands… and look so ruined under a shower?*
- *Why was fruit and chocolate more intimate than some sex I’ve had?*
- *What does “Access All Areas” really mean, emotionally?*
- *Can I live with these people?  They mock each other like siblings.  But they love like it too.*
- *Who the fuck am I right now?*

She chews the pencil. *Then underlines one.*
- *How to be a truth-teller in a world that spins fiction on instinct.*

Another page.  Another title:  **“The Duchess of Drumroll”**
(She’ll cross that out later.  Maybe.)

She scribbles furiously.  Starts writing a sentence that she knows will **end up being part of something real**.

*“You can walk behind the curtain and still never understand what it costs to hold up the show…”*
